Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue. Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates teaches us that the body is not the same without the soul as with it; and in the art of medicine also.

Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre. Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie. Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc. Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that because it is called the last of medicine, fire cautery; but behold; they do not believe that fire cautery is worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false; for it is the last of medicine because whenever we administer other remedies in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Certainly! Here is the translation:
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Indeed, here is the translation:
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	In any case, when you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is scorched by the color of the gold itself, and when it is too cold; and if you burn it too much; it makes a fire; and there is enough hindrance in this.

Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cautery methods are useful for moisture and cold, and are used in cases of a disease called "soda", and in cases of many humors that descend from the head as boils, and ears, and for many dreams and head and neck pain, and even for many diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by means of a medicinal solution modifying the head, either two or three times, according to what is useful and agreeable to the patient's habit; and then make the patient drink the head of the patient again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his feet; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his thumb between his two nails; and there or will come your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the nail then cover the cautery which is called "olivare", for this is the form:

Then cure the wound of the bleeding which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.

After the treatment of warming, when he is sane; and if you see that he makes no progress with the medicines I have written or if you wish to dose the treatment with additional medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is as follows. Shape the cautery like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called “closed” because its head is made in the shape of a nail or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small appearance; put out the painful limb, and hold your hand steady and lightly touch the fire until half of the thickness of the hair is burned; and hold your hand away from the artery, which should not be burned, and there should be plenty of blood.

After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, take it out; then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and cure the limb until it is healed. de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, take it out; then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and cure the limb until it is healed. And if you are going to cauterize this embolism with the cautery called "cultellare," at the very tip, keep the artery in this embolism that is not ancient.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cauterize an embolism as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cautery must precede medical treatment and that it does not suffice, then you must avoid the cautery called "cultellare" as long as it is blunt; and sign out the limb by drawing a line a half inch long, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and do not move anything until the bone; and be careful of the jaw that it does not move when you move, and that it does not cause you pain, and be careful of the displacement of blood from the artery when it is cauterized, or when it has been cauterized for a long time; and that you do not do anything rash or beyond your knowledge, and that you are not a student or an experienced physician; and leave the work in progress; but I will tell you how to retain blood when the artery is cauterized, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans. Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those which move with phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery which appears to come from drying and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture which is made of fumes of hydras and vomiting of head and gargling, and this is not worth it, then you must cauterize the patient with two cauters: one at the root of the ear, and the other at the temple, and the third at the junction of the two upper eyelids; and put the cautery on the part which is open safely, and make the cautery in the place of the head of the ear below a little below the corner of the eye, and another in the temple as long as a bean; and leave the cautery on for as long as half of the current is burned. This is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you cure the like of a cat o’ nine tails which we have put before you, but it is a more subtle and effective remedy that the knife should be a larger one; after curing thus as I have said above, until it is healed.

de litargie	De litargie.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	From litargie.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is sane, it is good; and if not, do two cauteries on the head, descending juice until it reaches the collar, and leave an inch of space between each cautery; and cure as with the others. de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head.

de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy

dou poil qui point l’oil	like those that prick the oil.

Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent. Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil. Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hair grow long and even, then make a parchment of the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live chalk, each a third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly, if it does not cool down, and put on the shape that you have made like a myrtle leaf, and put on the master’s eggs; and if the patient suffers only from oil, if you must operate in oil, and if there are two of them, put on the cotton wool soaked in oil; and the patient’s head should be in its natural position and put your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once or twice every time the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for he feels the bite as well as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have performed this for a long time, if the bones are stiff with medicine, you must have it.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the medicine has passed, if you lift the limb high, and you see the marrow rise just as it did rise by the constriction of fire or by incision; and if it is firm, it is well. If not, if you repeat the medicine on the limb or the medicine has not worked, until your works are even, and your eyes are fixed; then put on a wet cloth in the wound until the worms have gone, after curing the limb of the swelling which is called "dyafenis" and the like, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you must take great care of your work so that it does not bleed, and if the marrow becomes soft after, and the hair prick in the oil, if you repeat the medicine on that limb which has become soft from the marrow properly, just as you did before; after that cure until it is healed; and that is the form of the fuelle dou mirte.

de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size, and according to that be their constraints; and do not respond to him the right way to him who is the student of this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	And know that when you cure fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your cure does you no good, then you must burn it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in order; and hold his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, do not lower his head; afterwards put a piece of cotton soaked in oil of vitriol or in vinegar on the wound; then burn the cautery which is part: and touch it to the wound as if it were a feather of goosefoot, gather it up so that it is worth the work.  If you see that the wound is pointed from one side to the other, or if you see that it is as if a thread were torn; but in any case, that which is touched is more worth than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells out, and in its course it becomes soft and dry; when it is closed, if the swelling, and in its course it drives out the hair; after that, put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part where there is no feeling in the neighbourhood of the oil, so that your hand does not tremble; and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and compress it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good. If this is not the case, if you must do it again once, and another time if necessary, and leave it for .iiij. days; after that, put on moist cotton in the wound and cure the drying of the desiccant until it is healed, and if .xl. days pass and it is not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is discovered; and leave as it comes in this chapter
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mention. When there is a fistula, and you open the cavity; after that, put in the wound one small spoonful of camphor, which is like this in shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it in the amount of a third of a palm; and hold your hand or forearm firmly, and the patient does not move a finger, until the melted wax drains down to its oil; and it is fitting to put on the oil to the patient a soft cotton swab in the palm of the hand or on the forearm. The wax if it is too hard makes a fistula, and the same for mere curiosity without any benefit.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, that is good. But if not, if it is necessary, one must administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to the body in accordance with what is proper in each case.

Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are fractures in bones that are called "hair" and sometimes in limbs of children.

de l’aposteme de la goule	to the apex of the shoulder
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the swelling comes up to the root of the gullet or the eye, or the palate, or the root of the teeth, after that it must be perforated and drained and becomes filled and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not be of any benefit: therefore it must be that you cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or back; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would do in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the swelling comes up to the root of the gullet or the eye, or the palate, or the root of the teeth, after that it must be perforated and drained and becomes filled and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not be of any benefit: therefore it must be that you cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or back; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would do in its chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you must cure it with medicine and that will be of no use, therefore put the patient’s head in your hand; after that wash the cautery which will form later on in part as if you were putting on a pin; and put some cautery inside the tooth immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that let go of your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and rinse vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part for this reason, when it is confirmed that the limb was moving, the soft tissue softens and contracts, and the moisture becomes dry.
de la dolor des dens	And in part for this reason, when it is confirmed that the limb was moving, the soft tissue softens and contracts, and the moisture becomes dry.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures are of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the burn and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If the burn is such that you take a burr of beech, and put the end in a spoon of iron or steel; then take cotton and wrap over the point of a needle, and moisten with oil, and put over the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cool; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth.  And if you see that there is too much moisture and cotton on the burr, take off the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is like taking a burning iron or charcoal and holding it against the patient’s tooth; let the fire burn until it shrinks, then place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be great from the same or the next day. And it is believed that the patient should fill his mouth with soot in the haste of this cautery, and then remove it forcefully; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Do as you please with the cautery, and according to what you are able; and this is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	of scrofula.

de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that swells every limb, and when pain originates from the bone itself, that is when the sufferer cries out "podagre" in pain; and when the cause is cold and the disease does not yield to medicine, if it is cured by cautery in part: make a mouth of cautery around the joint of the limb, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion:

When there is need to prick the face of the limb, if you do cautery all over the cautery is claimed "point". de la routure dou syfac	From the root of the scapula
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones descend as coions, it is new; if you see it cured, do not trust that it is healed; and if it uses things that release its belly, so that the pain descends from its belly; then make it sit on its buttocks between your hands, and command that it hold its flank until the bones are repaired, and keep it still at your thighs, and mark with a sign on the edge of the fracture above the collarbone, and do all that is like half a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery like this:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Until it is soft and it feels sensations. Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. And when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in no limb</start_of_turn
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from sitting or from any other cause, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is advised that it be cauterized with the cautery known as "poins," or with such cautery as is appropriate for the length of the limb, its width and weakness, its flexibility and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat it. Indeed, it is customary that it must move towards the limb that is nearest, because it is believed that thus one can make the cauteries as long as the patient remains healthy.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, or from sitting or from any other cause, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is advised that it be cauterized with the cautery known as "poins," or with such cautery as is appropriate for the length of the limb, its width and weakness, its flexibility and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat it. Indeed, it is customary that it must move towards the limb that is nearest, because it is believed that thus one can make the cauteries as long as the patient remains healthy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The disease that proceeds from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy is never cured by cautery alone, and even the sickness itself that comes from the decay of these humors. When you see that the disease is at its beginning, take warning and cure it as we have said in the preceding division, and do not linger, for if you doubt that the corruption has spread throughout the illness, then make five cauteries on the head: that is, one on the forehead at the nose, and one on the front of the chin at the end of the beard; and two on the two corners of the mouth, and one behind the ear; and leave the hand as high as the cautery goes up to the bone, and as long as the scales fall out so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize on the wrist as it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is a general looseness of the humors throughout; and it becomes manifest, as it is fitting that you should cauterize with these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, that is to say, cauterize on the low side of the neck, and two on the spine of the shoulder, three on the spine of the back, and one great one on the armpit and one other below, two on the two scapulae, two on the flanks, two on the tendons of the wrist and hand, and one on every joint of the fingers and toes, and on the fossae of the hands; and be wary of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the heel or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And as many as you make cauteries, the more you will render aid, and comfort to him; and as many as the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as when he feels it, for he has already become corrupt. And it is fitting that the cauteries be great and small according to the limb and the joint, according to what you have learned in the handling of herbs. After curing the body several times with flour and honey and other cures until he is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils and plasters, and is not completely healed, then one should make cautery on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery be performed at a distance from the bone. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be done on the hand, foot or back, at the exit of a nerve that makes the limb numb. And if it is a bone that causes the swelling, nothing should interfere except for those who are skilled in bones and the issues of nerves that move the limb.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils and plasters, and is not completely healed, then one should make cautery on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery be performed at a distance from the bone. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be done on the hand, foot or back, at the exit of a nerve that makes the limb numb. And if it is a bone that causes the swelling, nothing should interfere except for those who are skilled in bones and the issues of nerves that move the limb.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine has no power over it, then one should make cautery with a needle at a distance, according to the thickness of the swelling, until the blood is seen to bleed, and let it bleed; then cure with flour of wheat from time to time, with lentils and rose oil, and plantain leaves, and colon and aloe, half of each; mix them all together and bind them with a bandage, and leave it until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre first starts, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery which seems like a circle, put all around the circumference of the chancre. And all the wise men say that one should cauterize also in the middle of the chancre; and all those who do not think so do not seem to me to be right, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already had enough of that; and the most right thing is to cauterize all around, at the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When any man hath a disease which is called "adubelati," and it tarries to die or by the excess that it doth make or by the evil of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and there is little blood, or by the tension; and thou seest him haste to die: then thou cauterize round about the mouth of little cauteries by pricking; afterwards thou leave him alone. For she will haste to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if thou seest her perish with all the cautery, if thou dost burn the cautery too much: this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put thy hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" while the cautery has perceived the pain, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels relief in part as much as in the course of the corruption be joyful. Afterwards cure him until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The burn cure by iron. Another method of disease that is called "corrodens" and is nothing but the weakening of a limb, for it causes the limbs to swell as much as the flames do to dry linen. If you see this disease in a limb that can suffer from an overall burn, then cover the small and great nails closely together according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; then burn all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains but bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the burned limbs and burn with oil until the burn blisters are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of the wounds that remain. And if after two days the wound has not healed, it is good; and if this is not the case, repeat the burn on what remains of the corrupted limbs. This weakening is never cured by water medicine instead of fire burn; but every burn is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of water medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The burn cure by iron. Another method of disease that is called "corrodens" and is nothing but the weakening of a limb, for it causes the limbs to swell as much as the flames do to dry linen. If you see this disease in a limb that can suffer from an overall burn, then cover the small and great nails closely together according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; then burn all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains but bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the burned limbs and burn with oil until the burn blisters are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of the wounds that remain. And if after two days the wound has not healed, it is good; and if this is not the case, repeat the burn on what remains of the corrupted limbs. This weakening is never cured by water medicine instead of fire burn; but every burn is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of water medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece breaks through the belly, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing feared which boils up from the belly. And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways. That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is done if one is reckless. That is to say, cauterize as though it were a nail of a sponge, and do it with good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the belly of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; then put all around the belly, and hold your hand tight around the belly until it comes to the front of the belly; and leave it there for two days until it begins to discharge pus; then make an poultice of wild mallow broth with lint, and leave the poultice on all night, and close the wound carefully and remove the dressing. Then cure the belly by applying pressure until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If it is converted by belly-pus, and many times happens in hands and feet, if one should consider that one must bring hot water cautery; and this is in part a remedy: take a needle of spider or iron, or a nail of sponge, and put it on the wound and the edge of the wound; that is to say, put nails around it; and put the needle on so that it embraces everything, then put some warm oil, and hold your hand well, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the needle comes to the root of the wound, and can find the hot water going deep just to the root; and give the patient a sip of the hot water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will discharge all at once from all its roots. So do another one, until you have cured all that is at the source, and then cure the wounds that cause swelling.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When the limbs tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other, if you command .iiij. cautery or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between the shoulder blades; and .i. cautery or pinch, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the healing of the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When the limbs tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other, if you command three or four cautery marks on the spine of the back, one cautery mark between the shoulder blades; and one cautery mark or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the healing of the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Never appear by discharge the body bathes, or pus that come from corrupt matters. If you order at the first time when they appear that you make a cautery on each head of the pus: a subtle cautery of nutmeg stick, from which the point is either grasped by the fire, or of aristegall root long, or by the lenticular cautery. And never cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they do not cross their edges forward, but are broken by the discharge from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there is often a great outflow of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is often a matter of great distress.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming down your thumb, and no blood comes out anymore; then take some olive oil cautery pieces, small and large as you like, until they are all red; then press [it] in, that is to say, large or small as is suitable for the wound and the limb in which the artery is obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as necessary.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out violently when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of another cautery that is already on the fire immediately.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the limb is restored; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and do this with such care that when the artery is large, it can be closed by itself without any other method than those we have mentioned: or by cautery, or by extraction if it is not treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to close the wound. And be certain to bind and strain afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb with tight draping or with the placing of hot things upon it, or other similar things, will gain no benefit from it unless it is of use in this case
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no remedy and no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still until it is healed from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that the wound is not frozen and does not swell and heal; and make inquiries of what is necessary to cauterize and administer medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said or in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or to apply hot medicine, and to inquire about the odium, the cause, the instruments, and the forms of the cautery; and in this chapter we shall speak of the treatment of wounds from the chest to the foot, and I shall deal with this matter in the same way as before, for it is easier for me to speak of these things in order.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must tell you, dear sir, that there is more peril and fear in this chapter than in the previous one concerning cautery, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not be rash. For from many people come cures. If they come from those who have suffered so greatly from their disease that they move lightly through fear of the disease, and from the greatness of their malice; of these things we must be wary.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are those who make you understand it, saying: "Wait, I am aware"; and the disease is desperate. It does not suffice for me that you yield only to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not be rash but thoughtfully of that of which you are certain, and of which you have proof; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either achieved or converted; and this will help you to acquire lasting fame, glory, and memory over time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you are doing well to understand and to grieve, and if you are stirred by the Holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selon ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’à piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have ordered from the chief until the foot, because you will find it lighter than what you have had to bear
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have ordered from the chief until the foot, because you will find it lighter than what you have had to bear.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease leave so quickly as in the countryside; and all those whom I have seen with it grow desperate. For this reason, it seems to me that it is worth omitting the work in parts for the cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have often seen children in whom the head of the shoulder was dislocated by moisture, and the head grew so large that it could not be supported; and there was such great moisture that it became blood, and this moisture if it is collected between the bones above the elbow and the bones below, and the work is done when the moisture is between the elbow and the bones, and the incision is small, that you must make a large incision; and it must be as long as this moisture has lasted.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture swells the bone, and you see the teeth of the jaw protruding outwards in a portion, and there is an acute pain when you press with your hand from within, and this does not subside: if you suspect that the jaw is fractured, make two incisions as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, drain out the moisture forcefully. After draining, tighten the edges of the wound with strips and sponges, and apply wine and oil, and leave for five days. Then remove the dressing, cure the wound with sutures and ointment, and leave the jaw elevated. Give the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.</start_of_turn>
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to look or open the opening of the abscess, and the collection of fluid; for never is it before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.</start_of_turn>
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides murió dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.
de reume	If the vein or the artery is opened, and the liquid is instilled, and you do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; and let blood flow freely, so that the patient does not die from excessive bleeding and discharge of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no other disease which is called "catarrh" which has pus or swelling, and when the disease is old and medicine cannot cure it, then the only cure is to cauterize with that which will cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	When you must join the bones again, do not cover the patient’s face; after that, wet the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open; then stretch the patient’s neck all the way with the cloth; then look to see if the vein has bled, and the blood from one side to the other is after the ears; then they are restored; then sign the marks; then join the one and the other with a pair of fine tweezers as long as the vein reaches the bone, and that is as far as the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, loosen the tweezers from the artery and join at the top, cutting as much as two thumbs together.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is joined, if you do not hold it steadily, it will immediately burst.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on examination, if you measure the quantity of the space of two fingers' breadth, then mark the point and proceed until you reach the bone; and what you must do is apply pressure if it is more than two finger-breadths, or less. According to what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the wound that you have made does not bleed, then strain the wound and tie it, and leave it to heal.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on examination, if you measure the quantity of the space of two fingers' breadth, then mark the point and proceed until you reach the bone; and what you must do is apply pressure if it is more than two finger-breadths, or less. According to what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the wound that you have made does not bleed, then strain the wound and tie it, and leave it to heal.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient secretion comes and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and the chalor in the temples and the old saliva forsened and similar things, it is medicated by means of medical cures and all that does not help, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is as follows: if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating; and when it is opened, strain his neck the patient with some cloths, then wipe the area of no rough hair, and raise the area of warm water until the artery opens clearly; then take the sponge and that is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	The manner of extracting them is as follows: if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating; and when it is opened, strain his neck the patient with some cloths, then wipe the area of no rough hair, and raise the area of warm water until the artery opens clearly; then take the sponge and that is the form: first loosen the skin slightly until you see the artery, then pull it high with forceps, and remove it well from the hairs that are below the navel; and if the artery is subtle, if the vein has its tip at the junction of the shoulder, then close that part according to the quantity of blood that is lost. For if it is not closed, it will not jump out without doubt in all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from .vj. cubits, just up to .iij.; and if the artery is large, it is convenient to ligate it in .ij. loops with a strong thread of silk, so that no blood will be seen before the wound is sutured; and withdraw blood steadily. Then cut away the excess that is between the .ij. loops in that middle hour, and if you see that, if you wish, cauterize with a fine cautery needle until the blood is clotted; and that is the perfect remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful in finishing off moisture: for this reason it is of greater aid than moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the cavity with much cotton and make good stitches; and when one removes them, if one has cured with dry medicines which cause new hair and stitches, as long as it is healthy; and if without support of the artery as much as one does work, if you are in a hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use the cavity of vitriol and strain your hand, as it should be; and if you do not have this present, if you must take out the cavity, you must do so while the vessel is not frozen, and rise the cold water until the vessel stops moving, and strain as it should be; and what is more painful and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting from a third to a fourth of an inch, but the cutting should be well spaced to prevent it from lasting too long.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the joints a space of one inch; then when you have signified the nails, let the loop burn until it reaches the bone, and close the vein with two nails; and let them be spaced between the joints, for they are not firmly joined by this cautery in all cases; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	And must have between the joints a space of one inch; then when you have signified the nails, let the loop burn until it reaches the bone, and close the vein with two nails; and let them be spaced between the joints, for they are not firmly joined by this cautery in all cases; and this is the form of the cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are above the test of the chief of force, and it does not profit from any medical cure what is done, and you see the face of the patient to become swollen, and to feel or front ambulation as if of fear; and so are they tense and moist if the paper tissues are held together, and are shaken by the heat of the tears, if there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the ancient 'cure contuse'; and you must make the patient who has this disease leave the hair long either front or back, then make two incisions or an even front according to the length of the front; and whether one incision is like two thirds of the way down the front swallowing the juice until it reaches the jawbone, and the other like one third has two ribs underneath the paper, and keep the incision of the arteries that are like two ribs underneath the paper; and hold your hand at the continuation of the two mandibles, and if there is a wound of any quantity at the place of the traverse joint.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have shown a piece of sponge and wipe the blood from his wound, then hold the sponge firmly for one-third of an hour in this way:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is at the root of the temple until the second incision; and scrape away all the marrow which is between the two incisions to the outer side of the bone, then make the other half of the wound until the other second, and then remove this sponge.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", which is very well-trenched on one side and on the other is soft, do not trench, for that is the shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", which is very well-trenched on one side and on the other is soft, do not trench, for that is the shape. And place the cutting edge towards the marrow at the shoulder, and the soft edge towards the bone, and hold tight until it reaches the middle fissure. And close all the blood vessels that descend from the chief as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the shoulder, and then do the same from the middle of the fissure until the other edge; then withdraw the blood equally, express the bone for the blood taken; then put into the wound a patch of cotton about the size of a finger, and put on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and wool, and keep that there are no after-bleeds. And after three days remove the dressing and mix in strong herbs of rue, then treat with basic oil of rose and other treatments like wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou reume des eulz	because of repeated bleeding
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is used, you see the pupils tense and small, the vision blurred, and papers burn; and the hair grows, and when it is plucked, there is severe pain, and the patient coughs; then blood comes from these accidents, from many veins, and the cure is that which is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc.
