Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When the patient is commanded to raise his forehead, then make a large incision from the left temple to the right temple, and another one wide. That is to say. From the beginning of the incision on the left temple to the bone; and pull away the hand from the nerves of the temples that move in the cheek; and when the bone is discovered, drain all the blood with a sponge, and then remove between the two layers of the incision and put in cotton wool, and try to hold in place; then cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep warm; when it is solidified, it is said that you should rub the bone until it begins to grow, and then cure with drying things that make it swell.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In part: take .ij. parts of rue flower and .iiij. parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds to make swelling disappear throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is found in the ear is either grains or best or stone or metal; or seed such as peas, beans, barley; or something fluid such as pus or blood and other things.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear that does not fit into the ear, do not put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, if no violet oil or rue oil comes out, then proceed with extraction; and make the patient swallow and put cotton wool in the nose while he is swallowing, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear down. Many times this cure comes out by itself; and if it does not come out, we must extract it with fine tweezers. In this form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, we must extract it with fine tweezers. If it does not come out by itself, we make an incision of small double thickness; and if it still does not come out, we make an injection of laudanum and cut off the chief of the injection or pierce the ear very much, and stamp what is around the injection with butter if it comes out with the injection; and the pain often comes out by itself; and if it does not come out partially, we take hold of the olecranium and put on no instrument that may cause damage, and put a little plug of cotton around; then we press on the olecranium above the stone or whatever it is, and the pain comes out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in haste to make an incision, do not hesitate to pierce the earlobe along with the abscess cavity. In such a case, if you make the incision first at the crown of the head, drain blood in proportion to the measure of its virtue. Then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear downward, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fatty tissue or cartilage below. Make the incision as wide as a moon until you reach the bone, then remove the bone according to your ability, and extract the pus immediately to your mouth; and cure until healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If grains are swollen and painful, administer extraction; if it cannot be extracted, administer opium in the form of pounded poppy seeds according to this fashion:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	make an incision of that grain. But do not do this until you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with tweezers and extract the pus, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear is acute, then the patient must use at first cotton wool and fill the ear with much cotton wool. And let it be outside or inside the ear, if it leaps for this, it is good. If not, take many pins according to the length of your mustaches and hold them tight and steady, and push them into the ear; and put the patient one or two of his ears against the fire; and make the patient spit out one of his ears, and pull out the other from the other side, and pierce from one ear to the other ear; and do this until the ear is entirely let out; and if you see that it leaps entirely, take hold of one of the chieftains and burn the other until the most tender part is as red as the joint. Then do the rest of the joint until the ear is entirely let out, as we have said concerning the pin.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the stone, if it is of small size, like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, we must feel it, if there is danger of extraction of teeth; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you cure it as we have said in the division and or treat with distillations, and the cure does not benefit, if you must know that the ear is exposed to the sun: if there are no worms to be seen, if there are subtle teeth, and if there are none to be seen, take the tweezers that are like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let the dressing be wide and loose. And take a little more of the chief from the ear in proportion to the amount of suffering of the patient; then proceed with all the care. Do this often until you see it emerge. And if they do not obey to emerge, if I am pressing around the cotton wool as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, if you administer distillations that the ancients have proved useful in the incision of the worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let the dressing be of silver or lead, wide and loose. That is, small losses, and above all let there be distillations; and let there be pressing from this instrument of lead well made for this purpose. And if you see a splinter and wrap around the point immediately with cotton wool; then pour in your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the dressing, and put the dressing in the ear; and press from within the splinter to the bottom of the cotton wool, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or almost from the ear; and let the patient feel within, and let the distillations be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	... of the swelling of the ear.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some mark on their ear; and the same thing happens as we age from wounds or earwax buildup. These imprints never appear without leaving a mark on the ear, if we do not see them; and never is there any time when one cannot see them.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When these imprints appear without being seen, it is a sign of great suffering in many cases, and in this instance it is seen that you put the painful ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the pus, if the wound has all the surrounding pus like this, then it is formed like that.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be cautious both front and back all around, if the ear does not bleed; if the pus is of earwax or from a wound in the ear, if you have subtle bruises, and if the swelling is slight, as long as the tumor is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if swelling occurs in the ear, if you take one raiser of subtle size and burn a little at the fire, then put in or on the ear. If you feel the swelling which the patient feels grieve at the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a piece of cotton according to the size of the hole, and the moisture in Egyptian order.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this without delay until the wound is healed, or you take a piece of lint and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you see it fleeing from the ear, it is likely that you have pulled out the piece of lint and put in another piece of lint made of rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is bony; then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is discharge of blood comes, if you plunge a sponge and wring it out in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures which are useful for loosening the discharge of blood which are either to apply poultices.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the paper's char. When it comes out of the papers, the blood comes out of the eyes when they are moist and dry; if you extend them from their nails and from their roots, and support them with a spatula at their root; then take out the broken glass piece.</start_of_turn>
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without this, if the fire cautery is done with a subtle lentil, and it is cauterized afterwards at the incision, it is enough; and many times it is repeated, so that none of their roots remain fixed; and when they are cauterized by fire, if they are burned those roots and do not recover.</start_of_turn
de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in paper scraps of things that seem greasy in their form and hardness; and for this reason this disease is called "granulation," and is an assembly of large moisture in the body under and about the bones; the work is like this: take warm water if the granulation moves from one side to the other, and that is a light thing to know; then loosen the skin around the lower part lightly, then take tweezers and grasp the hairs, and pull. If you do not grasp it with the pliers, you will not grieve the patient; and if the split is large, if the assembly has a bone, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for it will come loose soon and cause pus.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulation descends to the depth of the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and stretch the granulation with tweezers, and pull from one side and the other; and if the paper is pulled out by the incision, it will not grieve; and when the granulation is grasped, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of that which causes pus until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is enclosed in papers of paper that are soaked in water; and this comes more abundantly in summer than in winter, and causes great thirst in the eyes, and they come out in the morning; and for this reason they cover their faces with their hands at dawn, and sleep, and their papers are wet on their eyelashes as they swell up and appear covered with exinach that bursts in the oil. And when you press your hand on the belly and feel the exinach between the teeth.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And thus the work is that the patient puts his head in its place; then take one cloth of linen, and make a loop resembling a circle according to the quantity of exinach in the upper part, then put it on; and press on your belly from both sides, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make an incision at the navel, about the size of a wound made to the vein; and do not make it any larger than the wound made to the vein; and stretch the leather as much as you can while you see the exinach. And in many cases comes exinach from the incision, like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tissue from the entire piece of charcoal between your hands at the flanks, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not touch the incision, that you do not go beyond the navel, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the dislocation does not spontaneously reduce at the beginning of the incision, if you widen the incision slightly until it opens; then grasp it as we have said, then moisten the drape in oil and water, and place over it, and strain of bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there are such people who burn and put on to provoke the moisture that is removed. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the vein bursting out, if you cure the abscesses that form as much as it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs attached other than their natural state, and are enclosed, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases like tears that are accustomed to flow and soften papers and gum, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the fire cautery, or it is done by incision and suture or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the chief of the patient in your left hand, then draw the paper from the oil at your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a hook at every thread of the paper; either cut the edge of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs, and take out one thread from under the paper, and draw it to the end; then make in the lower part of the paper, the hairs attached, at all the breadth from the great tear to the little one; then take out one thread and put under the paper a little patch of cotton and bandage, and sign on the paper a figure like that of a thrush, and all that is necessary is that the figure be according to the quantity you see that the paper that is destined to you is elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a part that has to stay with a great quantity of paper according to what is seen; then make at all the breadth of the lines that you have signed, and from the great tear to the little one; and if there is one of the incisions close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then draw the ointment in one of the two angles of the wound, and burn it all; then gather the two layers with a suture of a needle with every thread of silk, and wipe away the blood, and do away with the excess of threads on the two sockets of all things sticky, as you see that it is done; and if you do not see that it is done, if there is no remedy, then leave the suture and the threads until the second or third day; and then cure the wound with sutures of dry and constrictive things, because the paper returns to its place at the support of the wound and its gathering, but the suture is useless (as they say the ancient ones), and that is laborious;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure which is as much like the fuelle of the myrtle as we have told, as in this: two oncomers must discharge in conformity with the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold this that which is above down with small forces equally in conformity with the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the stay, and the thing is not even, if you take a needle or there is some thread, and you hold it with the mark; and you take another thread and loop the great loop, and the second loop the small loop, and assemble between your two the threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the leather above where you have marked, as we have told, and then assemble the two layers of the wound together by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply some cerate and some similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hair of the armpit has been converted: if you do as we have said concerning incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for armpit hair is as follows: convert the hair and fat according to what has been said, then make three hairs by art, and three fine threads as long as the hair and as wide as a span; and hold two threads of each hand. Then assemble the one and the other securely over that which covers the oil of the hair, and strain the three hairs from the three parts. Leave for a few days, and the skin which has been strained will wither and darken and will fall out, until it comes out by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the hair has grown strong, then cure it until it is clean; and when the wound is healed, and if the hair has fallen out, it will not grow again. This is the form of the three hairs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is immediately a thread of silk subtle; then assemble the threads and know each one from the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be equal; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not touch the chief of the thread; then place the patient's chief in its place; and let go of the sun if the work is completed, for this is a subtle and minor work, then withdraw the needle at all the chase to the root of the hair to the joint; and make it pierce in the membrane as much as you can until you have pulled it out from its natural position; then draw out the hair until it reaches the chase, and withdraw the needle from the chase if there is one or two or three or more; then draw out your hand until the vein is completely withdrawn from the chase with the natural position of the hand.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from its piercement through sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair has healed in its place and the wound has closed.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this ailment called "aleacrati" or the rotting process comes to light, if there are two causes: one natural, and one unnatural.  And it arises from an wound, or from a burn or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of working in this case is that you make that suture, dry the flesh, put in stitches of linen, and leave it until it is healed; and do not use anything but drying and restrictive things. For if you do this, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there are softening things to be added, such as fennel; and alum or salt and linseed oil should be cooked, and dissolved in no oil, and it should wrap around a bandage, and treat this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from its former shape; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except in addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	De la char qui vient en l’oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is called «axacrati» naturally and accidentally occurs. The accidental cause comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of progress in this matter is if one grasps an awl, because it has a double thread, and the thread is in the flesh, and it causes the left lower eyelid to swell so much that the thread of the vein is split in two at the level of the eye; then the flesh of the cheek is elevated from the whole awl, and the pupil is dilated to one-third of its normal size.</start_of_turn>
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pupil returns according to what is commanded, that is good; but if not, if one takes a burr and puts it in the incision, and turns the pupil, and makes two incisions or cuts within the pupil; and if there are two incisions at each of the two angles of the incision that you have made, or if you make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the letter which has not ‘j’grische’; then hold that cheek, according to the quantity of its cost and disease, of that which teaches the pupil, and then join the two parts that are loosened, and tie with a thread of linen; then cure the rest as we have said of the mollifying medicines and the tents, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions. dou soudement de la papiere	If the disease comes from a fracture or sprain, or from cautery, then it is to be known that you must make a full incision of the hair with paper; and according to what has been said above; then remove between the two leaves of a book a tenth of an inch, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons will appear to be very learned in all sorts of things as to how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done in the work and the instruments in greater disposition.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the oil of the unguent.

des voines des eulz	Des voines des eulz.
