de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The disease which is called 'alcunnati' is not fierce except for the swelling which is made in oil, resembling descending water, which is not true; and the manner in which this swelling appears is that if you make the patient sit on a chair which appears and is straight, then take hold of his head between your hands, and move him as much as you see the swelling coming down to his eyes; then either bind him tightly, and do not let him descend and break the light, and see the patient do the things as he wants; and if it does not descend spontaneously, as we have said, make a scar and it will descend like water, and the patient will see the swelling as if it were water. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the wound. That is, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner of the wound and the crown, until the swelling is gone; and when it comes out, distillate in hot oil mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fennel and honey, then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the belly of the oil bowl.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis serre l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. Se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, when the water returns for the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is securely fastened and does not rise, gently pull the almagda loop slightly towards your hand and hand back; then put in some salve again. Then put over it a cloth soaked in rose oil and a generous amount of eggs, and bind with the healthy oil.  We and those who are with us put on a coat of broth with a generous amount of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda does not manage to enter the oil because there are parts of the limb that have too tough hair, then you must take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctive membrane alone, and do not linger too much, but make a slight incision, then put in alum, as we have said; and when the work is finished appears to the patient a sudden sleep, in which he sleeps on his back for a week; and let him be without any movement, and take nourishment, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him still according to his disposition until the seventh day; then remove him from this house into the same darkness, and let him breathe, and make him see nothing, and then put him back in his place until the seventh day; and do not do this at the time of the operation or after the incision, but it is necessary to give him something to eat, for his pain will rise very much.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And thus comes the oil out from the wound, so remove the bandage before the seventh day, and bring in that which soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, remove the eye and put on his face a little bandage to cover any opening, and keep it in this house of darkness. And then go out of the house and come in, and he turns into his case; and let the attendants know that no one must approach him in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Yrach who said that in his peace he had seen an alum of blood perceived, when the water succeeded the pain, but he had never seen or read of such a thing in our land or in the books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of almonds, for those who do not know them; and they are like peas properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their tops are of this same smoothness, and their backs in two angles like a goosefoot.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	like the head of a goose.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Like the head of a goose. Sometimes new or old hairs appear like scorpions with teeth; and if there are such or if the hair is entangled with blood-red colour, or if the hair is like soft bone colour. In those where these hairs are soft and not entangled, you must make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; and cover his nose, and spit the blood onto those hairs, and drive them away; then take hold of what you please to support under the thumb of the right hand, until you believe that the hair is entirely detached.</start_of_turn
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains, if the wound has all its edges loose, if nothing stays in place; and if without support it breaks away, or is undermined, or if it is an abscess, then take hold of it as you would with a burn; and if it is malignant, burn it away as quickly as possible until it is quite black, and leave the charred parts untouched.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the wound does not hold and moisture comes up to the palate, the teeth that are loose become sound; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, the teeth that are under the bone become loose; so it is necessary to put a thread of linen, about the thickness of a thumb, between each tooth; and to tie the teeth together with the thumbs and index fingers of both hands, leaving about the width of two fingers between them. Then put the patient’s hand over the thumb of one hand and the thumb of the other hand over the other thumb, and grasp the one after the other, while keeping the thumbs together. Do this until you are sure that the tooth has not been damaged. Then draw out the thread, wipe the wound, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and put the tooth back in its place as before. Do this for two or more days, until the tooth has healed over everything that remains of the root. Then put in or extract a plaster splint for several days until it is healed, and if necessary use calming medicines; and this is the form of the instrument for extracting the tooth, from which we extract the oils and medicines or not.</start_of_turn>
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Or of silver or gold, resembling a large coin, if like a chain; and guide it thus. And if you see, make a closed chain, and the instrument will be flat to purge the tooth; and have one hand on the thumb of the tooth to hold it when we burn the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the arm a disease which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes great at its outset, so that it is visible to the eye; and for this reason it is necessary that you immediately compress at the beginning, and break the bone, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you wait too long to compress it when it is great, if you take hold of it too tightly, it causes great pain to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of great color, you can easily bring it under control, if you empty the patient and compress it without fear, and cure the limb with dry things that restrain.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound together
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hair that when the solution of continuance comes upon one of these cartillages of work, it profite for that, because in some homes. It is necessary then that this should not happen to anyone, if he looks that the wound is fresh throughout its blood; and then he should join the two layers at a costure, and cure until it is healed; and if the layers are already split from one end to the other, he must support all the parts of its curve until they bleed again, and then reassemble the two layers at a costure, and strain, and sprinkle upon it some dragon's blood, and incense burned; and put upon the powders a piece of supporting plaster or another supporting plaster that binds, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, and then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the costure is that you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said concerning the costure of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	from the incisions of the layers
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of the home, there are veins apposed like sharp grains of wheat, smaller and greater; therefore it is necessary that you return the veins, and make incisions above each knot, and grasp with tweezers and compress in the middle part; then employ the blunt end of the needle after making the incision of the vitriole, until it is no longer stained; and then withdraw the needle easily, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the hardness of the jaw bones.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens on the gums of the teeth that they become loose and the old people call them “albules”; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or blood clot; then take out the blunt end of the needle, or other astringent and drying powders; and if the gum comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	When the teeth are assembled at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are loose and rough; never are the teeth black and yellow and towards the front, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if you make the patient sit between your hands, and their shoulders are against your chest, and open the jaws or the gums split open, until nothing remains; and thus do you make blackening and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if you remove what is at the root at the first attempt, that is good; if that is not the case, if you must repeat the second and third time, until you have everything back in place; and the teeth that have been between the jaws must have various shapes because those that you remove to drive out the teeth have other shapes than those that are left between the teeth; and these shapes and others appear to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait a while before retracting too much, because it must not be made to move too much; because it is a high-quality substance, so we have no excuse for retracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to bear down, if you are certain that the tooth is loose, many times the pain will leave the patient; and care must be taken that it is neither too loose nor too tight, and make the tooth bear down; and whatever does not suffice to relieve the pain while the mischief persists, as we have already done for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that the tooth is loose, you must gently extract it with great force to ward off the gum from all sides; then the muscle will relax on the two sides and the pincers will be fixed; and keep the patient’s chin between the knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, draw out the tooth directly toward the front; and if it does not yield, take no forceps and grasp it from the root part lightly, and move it as you did before. And if the root is perceived and breaks, if you cover it with cloth, the gum or the hole will be damaged; and if the pincers are grasped too tightly, they will break from the grasp. You must moisten around the gum to soften the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first. And take care that you do not do what the ignorant layman do, who break the limb many times without any reason, and do not bring about what we have commanded; but bring about many times by the swelling of the root that remains, or by the limb that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the root is pulled out, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, forasmuch as they are mute at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double when you draw the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when you draw, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so as to hold securely.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root comes loose when drawing, if you must remove the soft tissue around it. That is to say, as much as it is softened, and then insert the tweezers which are called “algefri,” so that the head of the pin appears like a beak; and be made just like a file and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not yield to all these tensions, if you must, uncover the flesh entirely around the root and place the instrument which is called “althali,” that is to say, a palainche, for this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If force and bulk are not sufficient to break me, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, if you assist with all your instruments, for when the forms come they will follow.</start_of_turn>
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has just rained, for this is its form:</start_of_turn>
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let there be great and firm grasps to hold the bone, so that it cannot slip but can be held and moved; and then restore the limb with the appropriate medicine for this case, and if there is any fracture in the bone, even if it is small, if the grasp has held all the instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural course, and the shape is deformed, even in female patients, if it is suspected that the tooth has penetrated too deeply and is not properly aligned, and cannot be remedied: then it must be extracted. And if it is affected with the tooth, if you take hold of this instrument which has the shape of a small beak, resembling a file, and is made of iron without a cutting edge at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And you must hold the tooth firmly in the palms of your hands for the duration of the tooth’s extraction, and because of that do not move the others, and if it appears, you can limber it, if you file it with a file that has the same shape as this.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is just like when we file nails; and while you are filing the tooth firmly in the palms of your hands, slightly move it until it stops bleeding; then at the end there is no rasping, and if it has penetrated too deeply and it bleeds the tongue, if you limber the root as much as it is necessary, so that it does not bleed or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When teeth loosen, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient is unable to press against that which sustains them, you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is of no avail; for if you command them to be restrained with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and causes pain, but the gums do not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth coming into contact, if you take the thread and pass it double between the two front teeth, then place the teeth between the front teeth, if there are one or more, as long as you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, until it does not move; and let your thread be attached to the root of the tooth if it is unable to escape. Then hold the teeth in tension with tweezers, assemble them, and place them between the sound tooth and the one just mentioned, and keep it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it so that it can rest as much as possible, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, if you strain with another thread; if it persists and serves its purpose well, and this is the form of teeth and the arrangement of the two front teeth and the two rear teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you reset it in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let no other be between who is wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of ivory, and put it in its place or where the fault is, and strain it as we have said, and leave it so for a long time with constant tension
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	The tongue hangs limp and loose
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	The tongue hangs limp and loose,
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are often boils in the throat which are called "godath", and they are called by their proper name "ij amandres". And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not cured, take heed: if they are hard of little size and have a yellow colour, do not touch them with fire. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with fire, even for the discharge of blood; but leave them as long as they are painful, and then you will take them out, or they will break by themselves; and if they are white in colour and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover them, look first whether the boils are resting and quiet. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and stretch his arms to his sides, cover his mouth with his hands, and press his tongue down with all your might, as this is the form; and let it be of silver or lead as thin as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press his tongue down with all your might, as this is the form; and let it be of silver or lead as thin as a knife.  See the boil, if you see it, grasp the poultice and insert it into the abscess, and push it out further than you can. And do not take away any cloth from there, then cover the instrument with the thumb, as this is the form, that looks like a force; and when the chief is bent, one place over the other, and is very sore, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can hold the teeth firmly, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can hold the teeth firmly, know that this is the form:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I medicated a woman with a small abscess that was not in the throat, namely one abscess of little size; and she had such a tight grip throughout the throat that she could neither breathe through the tube that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and she died because of it. And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two teeth from their sockets. I immediately took hold of this, and put one finger on the abscess, then I forced out a large piece of flesh; then I repeated the procedure in the other socket where there was no tooth, and I closed the mouth and squeezed the tongue; after that I put the finger back in the abscess, and held one part, and only a little blood escaped from the other part; and when I had stopped bleeding from the tube in the throat, the woman was able to drink water and then wine, and she did not stop vomiting from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess gradually subsided, and filled up the space that I had evacuated, as much as it would. Then I closed the abscess and cauterized it inside the throat: from that moment the abscess turned around; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And thus is the swelling of the eye.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus is the swelling of the eye.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, for the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take alum, isops, origanum, rue, chamomile, ivy, and all of these herbs together in one pot, and put them in, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot put one instrument that is pointed according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	This cure is safer than incision, for the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take alum, isops, origanum, rue, chamomile, ivy, and all of these herbs together in one pot, and put them in, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot put one instrument that is pointed according to this method:
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened at the throat bone or fish spine, or no thing; if you therefore take care that you show what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instruments, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned in the throat, take that you make the patient vomit the sickness as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it comes out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie to the sponge a thread, and then transfix it; and when it comes back, if it is broken, and then draw it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take one instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can more easily enter the gorge, and keep the head lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not slip from your grasp, do not bite down on the bone inside; and must you take care that the patient holds the instrument, for it is likely that it is swollen or the thing is loose; if the patient swallows, or if he treats it fiercely with the entire instrument equally, as much as he is able.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can more easily enter the gorge, and keep the head lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not slip from your grasp, do not bite down on the bone inside; and must you take care that the patient holds the instrument, for it is likely that it is swollen or the thing is loose; if the patient swallows, or if he treats it fiercely with the entire instrument equally, as much as he is able.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And never is medicine the cure, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when that does not profit, then look at the patient’s tongue towards the instrument that I have told you of. And if you see the swelling, if you treat it with all your might, or if you grasp something subtle that is worth this. And if that is not worth it, take a tooth of rue and put it in the patient’s throat, then take hold of the tooth or bite down on the rue. And if the patient feels pain all over, then take a full dose of cold water, and cover the mouth and the tongue, and make the patient swallow frequently; and if you see that the swelling is growing, stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not yield as we have said, if you suffocate the patient with a piece of asafetida, with the instrument which I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will have its effect. And the method of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces, and let the dressing cover be covered with a gauze perceived in the middle, and in that hole is the point of the instrument; then you pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out only through the mouth; and the mouth will now swell, and if it does not yield, resume the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, and eat dirty and foul things, and do not drink water; and then it will surely depart by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is like this, which we shall treat the swelling with, if indeed we can see it, it resembles tongs with curved handles to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of a bird, and there is lime on it, so that whatever it grasps, it will not let go; and when you have seen this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the physician of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The wounds of the fistula are, according to what is remembered in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways that these occur. One is in its own likeness, and because it holds moisture. The other is when it is caused by the bones or is at the bone. For the fistula of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the fistula of the marrow is different from that which comes in joints, and the physicians have their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the fistula is not to be perceived, as long as the bone is dead according to its completion; and if there are some that must be perceived when they are hardened, and do not die according to their completion, like a fistula which comes from a joint. For when a fistula comes from a joint, and it is left while it is inflamed, by chance if the vessel and the nerve of the joint are ruptured, because of the contraction of that limb. Or the fistula is from the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is measured, if it has already reached the principal member; or it is from the foundation, if the perforation is not made as high as it should be; and it must only be perceived in a hardened fistula with digestion accompanying, except for that which is from the foundation, which must not be perforated, and must be along the inside, and there will come a fistula; and it will not heal until a great amount of time has passed.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure. dou chancre	Then strain the abscess for three days on the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the liquid alone until it bursts by itself; cut off the dead flesh by itself.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said concerning the appearance of carbuncles, how one must work upon them with medicines, and how one must shun the cautery; and we say that carbuncles fester in marshes, and cause great pain in their cure. The ancients say that when carbuncles are in their prime or can be scraped out like those which are in mammels, and in the gut, and in similar places, one must remove them at their commencement; and when they are great and old, if one cannot approach them, for I know of no remedy for them; nor have I ever seen any healed before me.

Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already spoken concerning the similarities of dropsy and its collection of water, and the signs of swelling are similar; the treatment by medicine is the same as for fire cautery when only the light is eclysed; and one must not touch fire in these two instances: that is to say, tympanites and hydrophobia, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when medicines are applied for the semblance of dropsy called 'eclypses of medicines', and the cure does not benefit, if you observe the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, as with vomiting and other things; if there is no touch of fire, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great strength and has only dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then one must work.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Hold the patient’s right arm in your hands, and press the belly downwards towards the lower part of the belly, then take the pointed tweezers as follows: Make three incisions each about a finger’s breadth wide, and do not make them too deep so that they can reach the intestine when inserted, and do not sew them up.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if dropsy is adhering to the intestines: if you suspect that it is in the intestines, make two straight incisions on the flank; and if it is due to liver disease, make the incision on the left side of the abdomen; and if it is due to bile, make it on the right side, and do not make the incision too deep so that the patient does not bleed excessively from the wound that is too weak to withstand it.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the leather with the instrument, and the substance, and keep your hand all the space between the leather and the bone just as when escorting the quantity of a nail or an egg shell; then pierce the bone until the space comes to the end of the tooth, and that is the cause of the pain, then withdraw the instrument, and that is the form of this instrument: And it is similar to a silver nail, and is made of iron or lead, and has on the part facing outwards a small perforation; or costs as much as one part, two parts, and three parts on one side, and one part on the other side; and the tip is cut off like a pen, and that is the form of the incision which the writers make to cut off the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the head of this lies the ailment, so that when the instrument comes to the pain, if you immediately lift it up from the instrument; empty out then one-third or half of what is in it, for if you empty out more than that which is convenient in that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he will vomit, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but emptying out in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and in accordance with what the instructions of the virtue say concerning the patient and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the pain, and it is retained now by the pressure which stamps the perforation that is on the socket, as I have said, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from this, and withdraw a small quantity of the pain.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this to no man, and guard yourself from using it until it ceases to linger; for if you doubt the patient, and you put too much water in, if the cure be of the burying of earth or sand, with water or sweat, and by the sun, and drink wine; and take medicines that dry, until he is cured, and cauterize upon the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do this to no man, and guard yourself from using it until it ceases to linger; for if you doubt the patient, and you put too much water in, if the cure be of the burying of earth or sand, with water or sweat, and by the sun, and drink wine; and take drying medicines, until he is cured, and cauterize upon the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born without a perforation in the belly, or if there is a perforation, it is small, or it is not firmly in its place. If it is necessary to pierce to such an extent that there is no longer any discharge of mucus, following this form: then put or pierce with a blunt needle, and bind and hold for two or three days. And when he wants to urinate, if you keep the closure closed, he will urinate, and then you can remove it; and by chance there is no damage, for the urine that comes out will not leave the closure closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the opening is small, if medicine be applied with a lead weight, as we have said, if it expands. He who has not the opening in his limb is blind, for none are born with the opening at the root of the bone, for it does not secrete before it lifts up; and it cannot enter except by that which is above, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies recumbent on his back, and the head of the bone and the hip are as wide as a thumb, if the opening is in the middle, as it is right; you must prevent excessive bleeding that comes often, and if it comes, if the discharge of that which discharges blood is stinted, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des pustules de la verge	of boils of the hip.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils onto the limb, and are an appearance of foul matter; and in them there are both malignant and benign ones; if you take them at their root, anoint them subtly, and evacuate them all out, then put on a wet cotton dressing in Egyptian fashion; then cure them with diafinicon until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is malignant, of dark colour and discharging pus, if you wish to remove it, you must cauterize it. When you have evacuated it, and if the boil is at the root of the limb, and has part within the bone and part outside, if you wish to extract the part within first; and when it is fractured, if you cure the outside, if you do not securely assure the limb that it is not pierced, there comes blackening and corruption in the limb or around the joint; if you wish, remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a dressing of beeswax and meal which is made of pomegranate bark and sometimes, cure it with other medicines until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if blood comes out, if you wish to cauterize the moon, do so as follows: With the cautery, do as is said above: in the discharge of blood and in corruption; and if the limb is crooked and retracted, if you wish to extract a bone, drink or pour out of the limb a fistful of lead, and urinate the patient among them; and when the wound is open to the head of the limb which had not been circumcised, or there is wound or incision, if you wish, then you must burn away the flesh with the cautery, as much as the veins are loosened, and deliver the limb from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If it is urgent to divide this, if you must, then cover the head of the limb with a cloth without any hair or nail; then slowly separate between two joints and put a wet linen bandage on with cold water, so that it does not slip.
de la circoncision	If it is urgent to divide this, if you must, then cover the head of the limb with a cloth without any hair or nail; then slowly separate between two joints and put a wet linen bandage on with cold water, so that it does not slip
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply a continuation of the ailment if like other wounds; however, since we are doing this work of our own free will, and properly undertake it, if it is necessary that we do it better, and the milder way for the health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old doctors did not teach me circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision to make a hole, and to force, and with all their skill; yet if the testicles escaped because there were two threads, and by chance if one sews up the lower and leaves the upper unsewn.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound closes again, and the pain is doubled, and there is swelling which is more than just a little discomfort; and by chance the thread escapes, and corrects the work, and many times comes out without there having been any need for it, and I have seen that.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made by force throughout the whole length of the thread, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces tear just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if it is held equally in every way, that is to say, that the thread should be thoroughly stretched from end to end; and that the manner in which you commence the work if you wish to make the child understand, that if he understands, you must not force him to bind the thread around the limb too tightly, but must allow him to do it as he pleases in every way
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then hold your hand straight out between your hands or from the toes of your feet that the child does not see them, neither any instruments; then put your hand on the limb and breathe or stretch out, and draw up as much of the limb as the head of the limb is taut; then thoroughly cleanse the wound that is put together, then bind the limb with a double thread, and bind it again from the inside outwards; and hold the thumb and the little finger together by the second binding, and press between the two bindings, then keep the thumb out of the way and draw up the limb.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood flow freely for a while, for that is the wisdom; and sprinkle powder upon and about the wound. i.e. a bandage that sticks with a piece of egg white broken from a rose petal, confirmed with rosemary oil good and fresh, and leave it on until it has healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	If the force of the limb is weakened in this way: let the two shoulders be tense and taut, and let the limb be as strong as the hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the limb is when the nerves are injured during the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your finger, even though it makes an incision; and hold it equally, and if you do not manage to hold your finger, if you keep it tense, and then let go.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass two days, and what is beside the navel is inflamed, if you leave them as long as the afterbirth is quiet, and the swelling is slight; if you touch them as you wish, and hold onto the navel, it will do you no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you touch too much powder to a wound, as we have said, or treat it with powders, and you touch it more than enough, and it swells up, if it does not heal; cure it as we have said before, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	Regarding the retention of urine...
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from the obstruction of a stone, or blood clot, or bile, or worms, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the previous division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine is not discharged, and you see that the obstruction is caused by the stone which is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, then you must command the patient to bend his knees; put the pieces of wood outside the back, extend his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move; and thus constrain the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is discharged immediately.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes,” for this is the form: either of silver wire slightly blunt at the end like the beak of a bird; or the caine of a palm of a long and a half, or wire of the finest kind.
