Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And thus it is done with the issuing of urine that if you take one and a half threads of a double, and bind one end to a chief of wool or cotton, and wind the chief through the syringe; and drain the surplus of wool and bring it up to the end of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and rosin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and the belly with oil moist and oily with olive oil and tepid water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the syringe smoothly into the belly, as far as it reaches the root of the belly; then double the belly upwards towards the buttocks; then draw out the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty, for this is not done except in this order except for the fact that it is guided or it goes crooked; then hold the thread at both ends of the wool and the urine follows the wool, and then take it out again, and correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are stones or blood in the bladder, or if pus is accumulated, and you see urine and medicines boiling over, if you do everything that is called the "clepsedre," which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if there is a break: two parts from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and it is held by that which you see. When the bladder is full, and the medicine is strong, and it is pressed, the moisture is pushed out, and the stone is driven out as much as possible.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see the medicines flowing in the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and draw out what is hindering; if you draw out the moisture from the catheter, and then push strongly on the catheter, if the moisture enters the catheter, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of a subtle blister from which one should clip the bladder: if so be it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from this there is a vein or a bundle of nerves; then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture which you see used to clip the bladder, and bind it between the two breasts which form a double bond, and burn the moisture upon the fire; then hold the head of the blister in the palm of your hand, and strain your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round; then hold a strong thread in these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division how to perform an incision of the stone, and the extraction with medicine; and we have mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that must be extracted; and in what case a stone must be opened by size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and concisely about them.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is retained in the bladder is oftener painful than when it is outside; and this is a sign that the bladder is suffering from excessive urine which resembles the suffering in its subtlety; and there is frequent straining, and the patient suffers great pain in his side, and he goes to the toilet many times, and then grows stiff; and from these strains the foundation is loosened.  And it is easy to cure these strains until they are three years old; and after that it is more difficult in old men, and is as bad in young men as in old; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is possible, first cleanse the patient with vinegar, to remove all the worms which are in the intestines. For they never fail to obstruct the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then grasp the patient by the limbs, loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; never fail to keep it low; then make him sit between your hands, and his hands should be resting on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then query and touch him there.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry now to cut above the stone. And if it does not yield to the toucher on the whole, if you think the patient is feeble, take your left index finger, if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man accompanying her; and press it down to its foundation, query the stone, and when you feel it with your thumb, if the bladder is full at the neck; then press above your thumb, and the stone will come out either by itself or as you see it cut.</start_of_turn>
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder to his hand, and command him to extend to his right hand the ribs above, and to his left hand bone the skin which is below the ribs in the part where we make the incision; then put the sponge in covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And command the minister to press the bladder to his hand, and command him to extend to his right hand the ribs above, and to his left hand bone the skin which is below the ribs in the part where we make the incision; then put the sponge in covering, as it is formed:
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and the press if the hand which is or the foundation, that it leap forward to work; and the sponge that there is part of the stone or it has angles, and margins: if it is grasped to irritate; and if there is part which is sweaty, like a gland, round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles and edges, make the size greater; and if it does not jump, know that you must grasp upon the nails which are as sharp as a file at the head, in order to grasp the stone if it escapes; or you will leave behind the instrument which is similar to a curved spatula at the head. If you do not manage to engage it, it will become large; that is to say, the hole will be wide, and if it does not go in without difficulty, it is the straining of vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there are more than one stone, grasp the largest one at the belly of the bladder first, then hold above, then pull out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are any. And if it is large, cover it with silk, and make a greater wound. For in this matter there are two things which happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out at the same time as the blood, for his wounds cannot be closed. However much you may try to drain, or remove the nails, as long as you drain them in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold, and put on above a moist bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the cautery; then raise the patient up on his heel, and do not remove the bandage until three-fourths of the day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, if there arises much pain like the smell of oil and water, then cure with ointment of diafinicon and ointment of basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If pus comes out of the wound and corruption, and blood clots in the bladder, or if the urine is retained in part like without leaping over the urine: drink plenty of wine in the wound, and take out that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and bring it about.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound gently and easily and support it, and give him help in every way that you can, until it is healed; and cover that all the times that you cure it, that you bind the parts together with sutures, and assemble the medicines above the wound
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urine passage, and it is firmly fixed, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician performs what I have said above, then you must know that it is of great size for this cure. I have seen this proven to be true in many cases.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the iron as described above and be at a right angle with two handles fixed at a distance of one thumb:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the edge of the stone so that it does not go back into the bladder; then press the iron lightly against the edge of the stone until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron towards the hand towards and away from the body, as much as you can see the stone from the other side; if the urine comes out, then press your hand against what remains of the stone which is in the bladder. If it breaks, and spurts out with the urine, and there is blood, then know that the patient is sick;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you are unable to do this, grasp the limb firmly by two fingers, and then place your thumb between the two fingers and grasp the limb at its base. Then pull the limb out forcefully, loosen the ligature, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you are unable to do this, grasp the limb firmly by two fingers, and then place your thumb between the two fingers and grasp the limb at its base. Then pull the limb out forcefully, loosen the ligature, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the limb is dislocated in women, and if this never happens, if it is cured, it is defended by two things: the first is that sometimes the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to manage her household, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman who is very skilled in this work of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman’s thumb is more thick than the man’s thumb, for in that case one can make a deeper cut, and there is greater fear of infection.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If necessary, if you take a small mark well knowing, and prick the flesh, and if you do not find it, not even a subtle stain; and present a woman who is skilled in life, or a woman who knows how to do a part of the work, and command her to do what you command with inquiry of the thumb
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and watch well if the woman is a virgin: then you must push back her skirt or foundation and inquire about the thumb; and if she finds it, if you constrain her foot, command her to hold her foot or with the patient, and press her left hand on the belly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If this be true, if you must move it with great force from the entrance of the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh; then close above the knee at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone which is often broken there, and feel the knee in that part; and do not move it up or down, and let its size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then stretch the limb to its natural size, if you feel the knee so swollen that the bone can easily break, and that many kinds of bones are like this: small and large, thin and thick, brittle and soft, long and round, and those that have rained. If bones look like this, it signifies an issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put on a wet compress, and hold it for an hour until it is dry; then return to your work, until the bone is healed, and have the instruments that I have told you about for extracting the bone as a helper in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go away naturally, and it is a severed artery, put powder on the limb and bind tightly with strips and bandages, and do not attempt to move it again; leave the wound alone and do not touch it, except in cases of great danger when the patient is in imminent peril. Then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the color of blood has subsided and the limb is relaxed, if it returns to its work, as long as the wound is still open.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the intestines.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is like lumps of wax, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not another act; and it is the skin of the egg between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this leech is from weakness that comes from the eggs, and it is spread through that substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the eggs, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and such things occur more frequently.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of the approaching disorder of this assembly, for if it is white or yellow like we have said, if the abscess is round like the head of a nail, and does not yield to the touch, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	If there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a portion of the yolk, and because of this it is believed that it is another nail;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If the moisture is between the leather of the nails and the yellow, if one feels it well; then when you see the colour of the moisture, if it is like the surrounding matter, thus is its form as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, following the introducer, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if it is known that the patient is sound, according to some, and the swelling of his body; then we lift him up on his back, on something rather high, and put cloth under his armpits.</start_of_turn>
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the limb towards one of his ribs, between the ribs and the navel.</start_of_turn
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then we take the sponge of leather, and grasp the skin of the ribs among the ribs down to the navel, and make a cut straight across the skin of the ribs until you reach white flesh, and withdraw it gradually as much as possible.</start_of_turn
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the face with a sharp needle through a large opening, and drain all the liquid, and then put on your gloves, and extend the face upwards; do not touch the root of the teeth, but only the face itself; cut everything or in pieces immediately the cost of its substance, for if you do not cut it well, the liquid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the upper jaw leaps out from its place during the procedure, hold it in its place until you have completed the work of the face; then reassemble the two bones of the jaw to their natural position, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the jaw corrupted by another illness, you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut the bone throughout its suspension, drain the abscess, and cure it like we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if it is acute, it is assembled in.ij. parts together, its roots that are.ij. branches; if it is pricked the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound wool soaked in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put away other wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on the.ij. nails, and put under doubled cloths, and bind on all the surrounding area according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take.ij. cloths, and use coarse wool like this and assemble them by stitching in the armpit, and one of the arms grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two fingers grasp on the.ij. angles, and be all assembled the restriction in the loop of the armpit.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this cautery of fire in lieu of the size of iron; and take only a superficial cautery, and burn the leather of the joints, and if it is eschaufed as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the juice is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and perforate that membrane as with needles, and scorch with this superficial cautery, burn:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And burn in all ways that you wish, until you have scorched everything; and keep that fire away from the egg; and keep that the juice of this substance is more salve; and take care that there be no evacuation of blood, and that you do not make any incisions of that size.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing else hinders you, or incisions of blood or discharge of blood or anything else, if you are to cure that which hinders you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is pale and faint, and does not wish to endure this work because of its horror, if you bring about perforation, as I have said, and you are certain by the indications that the aqueous humor is abundant,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then you must set the patient upon a low seat; then puncture the abscess at the lower part with a broad spatula, and put the perforation through to the bone; and if the opening is large, so that all the pus comes out, be quick about it
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the limb and bind it, and leave only the remaining pain to be cured; then treat until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white wool does not prevent the pain from leaving the wound, if you must, drink a penny or the instrument used to treat the pain of hydrophobia, as it is said above; and enlarge. That is, loosen the wound, and draw out the infection, and reassemble after about twenty days or until the wound is healed, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will be free of pain.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	from the incision of the veins
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The wounds that are in this part of the limb have many diverse dispositions, for it seems to me that the matter is worth leaving alone.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come or break, and I have seen this often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive heat and moisture, which is spread by blows or percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is of the colour of an abscess, like the colour of blood; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance it is a wound that is grievous and painful, and of foul colour, and never comes from any artery, or from a swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the position of the wound cauterized when you press it with your hand;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	Whoever causes swelling of a vein is known by his way of expressing it at the touch of the two [arms or hands].
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can make them appear of the same size as before, and on the other limbs as well;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you support the limb like a cripple, then the swelling will go up, and the white membrane will be released from the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the swelling has already been set with these supports, if you must then touch the swelling and support it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is loose at the socket, or inside the vessels, it is necessary that you deliver all that is taut, and gently round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage is loose at the root or behind, it is necessary that you grasp it all, and pull out the root, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you employ wool wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the heel of the foot.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is a wound covered with a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the edges.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain as he moves his hand
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this disease is very painful like that mentioned above,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and we will tell you everything about the treatment, as the ancient doctors did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is proper that you make the patient sit upright on a chair, and then support his head with your hands under his chin.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	Then seize all the blood vessels that protrude from the edge, and hold them firmly, and extend them outwards;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then grasp the soft tissue with broad scissors through which the vessels are exposed, until they are fully uncovered,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then draw out the clots from the corners, as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or if there is double thread, I bind it to the first root or where the vein has come loose, and I bind it to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I hold the edges firmly in the middle directly, according to the length of the bone, and I remove the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I treat the wound like the others or I bandage it, so that no vessel tears except for those that nourish the surrounding parts;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because in this way there is no harm, and if all the vessels come together, if you can draw the parts to all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the blood does not clot due to the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not move, it will not help.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the disease
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The event of this branch is by the section that comes or by swelling above the belly in the part of the flanks, for the intestines descend from that route to one of the buttocks;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	These four methods are caused by percussion, jump, bruise, or the lifting of grief from the belly; and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the sign that it is an extension of the shoulder, if there is some pain and some, in long tension, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the sign that it is an extension of the shoulder, if there is some pain and some, in long tension, and does not come immediately; and the scapula is parallel to the edge, because the shoulder presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the shoulder is dislocated, it causes sudden pain, and the scapula is displaced, from the stretching of the skin and the protrusion of the bone from the shoulder socket.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does blood flow with the intestines, and is retained when it is pressed, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, because it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And in these cures of fire with fear, because it is known to escape. And the manner of the work is that if you command or the patient that he hold his intestines to his hand within the wound, if he can return them
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either bind his bowels on his collar between your hands, and hold the buttocks;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the limb above, and grasp all the hair along the length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then from the depth of the wound, take leeches as many as necessary according to what you must do to open the wound, and if they are such that they cannot be withdrawn, leave them in place.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then withdraw the blood that is from the surface of the skin, until the white blood is discovered throughout;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then support your thumb in that which supports the bone, in that which is between the white blood which is from the surface of the skin and the second blood,
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and stretch out that which is behind the thumb, and between the second blood; and since move your hand forward of the bone of the thumbs, and extend the white blood up to your left hand, and keep the thumb to all the blood towards the size.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to extend the arm upwards, and loosen that which is behind the limb.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And if at your touch there is any loop of intestine or white fat that is hard, and if you find nothing, if the gut is in the abdomen below
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or there is a thick thread made of twelve threads, and pass it through the back part of the fat, which is behind the skin of the buttocks; after that the size, then cut off the ends which appear from the threads, until there are three threads left;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the fat, which we have said is behind the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of two inches;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then cover the head of the shoulder with folds of cloth, and bind them firmly in about a third of an inch, so that no vessel which nourishes them can enter there, except for the median nerve which must not be restricted.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And draw out the limb straight according to the first long line about two fingers’ breadth from this one, and after these two fingers leave space sufficient so that the fat which is like nails about the size of a large lentil fills the space;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	And afterwards according to the curve which the ear carries; then bind firmly in the part which is like the skin of nails, as much as it will stay in place, and bow it, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply a soft wool dressing soaked in oil, and put it on the wound, and I recommend applying the bandage that we mentioned earlier.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the fat surrounding the wound as we mentioned before, after the incision, in doubt of further bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the limb as long as it bleeds by itself; and if it swells up from a sudden hot bath, put on what we mentioned before, as long as it bleeds;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And if it is too late, the fire will only do more harm.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I have never seen anyone succeed in curing it with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old people say that it is made just like the limb that is connected to the vis, in part as if you bind the veins, after the size above loosely to the outside;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then hold it in the middle, and cure the abscess of that which causes the pain; and the cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never comes routine among the angry ones, as we have said, and open the doors; and do not leave any intestines inside, for if there are any, it is enough, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and all the time if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or the swelling, as long as the intestines are leaving;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this comes from the swelling of the swelling which is angry, as we have said, because it is swollen, then it is softened and the doors are opened
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; and never is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb from the root enfleated with two fingers according to the quantity of two fists.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then draw out the scab that is under the skin that covers it, then take the pliers and take out the limb that appears under the scab.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two thumbs that appear under the scab on the top of the pliers, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then draw out the limb, and do not cover anything with the scab or extend anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then cure with the treatment of wounds. And when you tie up the hair, if the moisture departs and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no mark in its course, and the burn is mute in this place, and more adjacent to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times is the skin of the nails softened in households, because the nails that are within are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when you see it cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then gather the layers together with a staple, and if you see that, close the excess of softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the hair.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des hermofrodites	Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, and for this reason I would rather not speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary for us to do so for two reasons: the first is that the patients themselves can respond when asked, and the second is that we have often had to cauterize beasts for our assistants, such as oxen and sheep and goats and others. I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.  In the former, we seat the beast in warm water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are firm and we can no longer feel them.  As for cauterization of great size: it is necessary to hold the beast steady, and to press the skin of the hairs with our left hand; then to bind the suspension, and to grasp each hair with our thumb and index finger, when they are well secured; and leave no trace of blood or clot on the vessels.  This method of cauterization is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction the beast desires to move; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in accordance with two manners: one if between the two testicles opens as with the figure of female nature, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine of the female. And the other manner if it is in women, and has on the navel as with a girl and two testicles. And the cure for the tumour and fame is if you cut off all the testicle stones, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a stone that is cast above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand, and this is the cure. It is necessary to keep the excess of the tenticle away from your hand or elbow, and to cut it lightly; and do not be too violent, for blood does not come, then the cure will be like for other wounds; and at another time when it appears at the mouth of the marrow, and the pain, and by chance spur out, and is like the semblance of a cow, and for this reason it is called the ancient "lame disease". If it is necessary to cut it out, as we have said concerning the tenticle, and the cure will be when it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	If the nature of the woman is not clearly understood, or if the opening is small; and if it is natural birth, or by accident through illness, or by pressure of the bladder, or by stones in the belly, or by any other similar cause; and if the conception, and the birth, and by chance the flowers have come; and if you have knowledge of this, if the period is close to appearing, if there are two eggs in the belly, or on the side. If it is a soft swelling and is close to the genitals, if there are two testicles close to each other, put the two thumbs together, let the woman lie on her back, spread her legs; then the two testicles will form, as long as the soft swelling is round, and is over the swelling; then take oil, and pour it over the wound, and put it on the body, and keep the woman still in every place where she can’t move. And if the swelling is hard and thick, if you must break it like a hazelnut leaf. If the swelling is of the bladder, if you suspect it at the navel and break it; have medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, incense, together with many eggs; then mix in a large dose of lard, so that the wound cannot bleed; and let it be long, and mix in a little attempt of dry lint. And if there is a stone in the belly, if you cover it according to this method, except for an inflamed appendix. For an inflamed appendix that is in the belly, do not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	Des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not accustomed; and when old, they become swollen; and as we have said in the division, their signs and symptoms, I will say here those which resolve cure. I say that emorroids and swellings, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the cure with iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the testicles tightly, grasp the head in its roots, then sprinkle over medicines which restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then put it into cold water; and if there is still bleeding, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take oatmeal, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one application upon her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is a wound at the back, and there are clots, take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make it bleed. And when the wound is healed, if it is a swelling which is called “albathir,” it is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the swelling; and then it will heal as well.

Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division. de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. The midwife first notes when the child naturally assumes the normal posture of an infant, and these signs are when you see the woman pressing down on the navel, and longing to smell urine: immediately the child bursts with desire to suck; so that his hands that were previously clenched now rest open, and when you see these signs, if you gently press his abdomen, if the child sucks his thumb, that is normal; for when he descends on his navel, if he remains with his thumb, he is overcome by the disgust of his superfluousness; and this is not natural. For it never happens from his toes, but from the stiffness of the limbs, or the hands, or from his belly, or from within, and is converted by chance from his collar, and from other vicious figures; if the midwife is skilled in this matter and subtle in these things, and avoids error and deception, and I will show you all the figures that help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child naturally descends on his navel, the woman gives a gentle push, and the child’s ability is weak; if she sits on a chair or the women hold her; and she should have an oily substance or rue to anoint herself, and then she should join the dance between her two thighs where she forms a small space.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	Et fend la secondeine, et coppe à son unguile tant qu’il moistures qui est en soi corrige fuers; et prend le ventre de la femme tant qu’il enfant descend, et s’il ne descend, si covient clisteriser la femme de muscillage de fenugrec avec huile de sisament; puis la fai prendre et esternuer de condisi, et tiens sa bouche et son nez une heure: si istra maintenant l’enfant. Et si les deux mains s’istillent vers le haut, si covient qu’on les ramoinne légèrement pour qu’elles puissent entrer; et s’il ne les puissent pas entrer, si met la femme sur un siège, et li garde les pieds en haut; puis déboute le siège sur la terre, et tiens-la, qu’elle ne crie pas au déboutement; et si les mains ne puissent entrer, et l’enfant meurt, si liCope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	And split the second toe, and grasp its nail until the moisture which is in itself corrects the fire; and take the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with fennel muscle and oil of alum; then make her take and spit out mustard, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if the child is now born. And if both hands twist towards the head, if you must that they are slightly remoulded so that they can enter; and if they cannot enter, if put the woman on a chair, and keep her feet high; then pull out the chair from under her, and hold her, that she does not cry out; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, if you grasp the hands at the ankle which is put forward, and pull out the child, and leave her equally.

de l’issue des gemelz	Therefore if it is slightly dislocated.

de plusors enfans	Moreover.

de l’enfant mort	De l’enfant mort.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman in childbirth of a dead child or belly, if as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained by the work of your hands;
