Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if you suspect that there is something wrong with the living child as we have said in the previous chapters concerning the matters of the sea;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	...and if blood comes out, whether from a restriction of blood or from other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had a child in her womb, and she consulted with one beside her, and refuted the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she came to have an abscess in her belly, which grew so large that it burst, and began to cause great swelling.</start_of_turn>
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to call for help, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the wound.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong dressing, and out came a bone, and after that a few days another.</start_of_turn
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at the mouth, for in this belly there is no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that this was the bone of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I want the wound, and with hands of bone, as long as the woman is better;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and saw the woman long tense with fear, and that was already a great blow to her.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have never seen this chapter except for the fact that when the master discovers a strange thing, he immediately seeks help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to restore the head of the shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, as we have seen in the books; and there are two returns as two blows of the hand.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the corners should be more subtle than restrictive, and be made of lead or bone;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And either the mouth should be open wide, that is to say two fingers wide, and the jaw should be wide, and long one palm and a half.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And in between the two limbs should be two cushions of the same size, which should be fixed one against the other, half a palm or more in length
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two cushions are put in the mouth of the basin to open when one turns the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of the nails;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And he has thus two joints of the armpits, if you see, of a palm's length, and two fingers wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you see the armpit open with all the instruments, if you make the woman sit with her legs drawn up and her feet over,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then hold the two armpits together in the armpit, and keep the chief of the instrument between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then move your hand over all the instruments, as if you have done with your nails equally, according to the quantity that you see the armpit open, until it boils faint.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when you behold them appear, the work hastens, and the higher your home is for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not expect the instrument until it appears, because its necessity is not dispensable
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second [tooth] is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to retain her lip, and then make her spit it out by condition, and hold your hands to the mouth and chin;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps for this, well is that.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot and make a hole or incision, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the mare, as camomile, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	If not, take one pot and make a hole or incision, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the mare, as camomile, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, be boiled or steeped in water over the fire; then put a scab or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mare’s mouth.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and hold it until the vapors come out of the mare; then make her cough, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is sprained,
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	If the second joint is sprained and remains after this treatment, and is not better, as the master commands, let her bathe her left hand in oil of sesam or in alum, and then put it back in its place.</start_of_turn>
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and let her grasp and stretch it out again, so that the mark does not bleed during extraction.</start_of_turn
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move gently to and fro, and then treat her; if she comes and dries out.</start_of_turn>
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is infected, as we said before, for its cure we recommend external drainage and the fumigation of herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	if it is not all of that we have said, if you do not follow our advice;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marrow, you bind to the hip of the woman, then cauterize with oil tetrafarmaçon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she cries and comes back, and comes out; but all the same, when she is well, if there comes a bad smell from the stomach and the head, and the patient groans.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it be certain therefore that fumigations are helpful in this case: neither of the ancients has proved the efficacy of fumigation with rue and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman is that we keep her at the retention of the flowers and the secondine if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is seen to be like a cat, and we put on the head of the instrument in the manner of a midwife, and the big hairs above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and either the fumigations above the charcoal, and the soot as long as it is consumed, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Whoever is born without perceiving the foundation has had it stamped upon him from the outset.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	therefore, if you must dance, so that you perceive that stamp at its place, and do not prick with any sharp object, and keep the lacement so that it does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a cloth soaked in wine and oil, and then the bandage until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, put or pull a piece of lead and leave it there, and be still as long as the patient sees a tremor in the bedchamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never comes this stumblement from the support of a wound or an incision; if you cover that support: if it be cured, as we have said of the lead weight.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation</start_of_turn>
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodules, and greater when they come from below the foundation deviate, or in the space between the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or more; and when that swelling is old, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture that oozes white or thick blood,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And in no case do these fistulas persist; and they are known by the fact that there is blood in the stool or vomiting, or by the patient's straining when they defecate, and by chance during a jump.</start_of_turn>
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and half the thigh; and reach as far as the hip joint, and as far as the coccyx bone.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus it is known that a persistent fistula is at its origin, and does not go away.</start_of_turn>
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite your thumb or foundation, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no distortion.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is distortion, if you insert a attempt of soft sponge, or hair of a horse, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair on your thumb;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no bleeding or vomiting or wind, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	The patches must not be torn; if you are in a hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or the urinary tract, if in a jump the urine spurts out, and cannot be held back by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is perceived up to the hip joint, if the vein is ever opened up to the body;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no swelling and the pain is not severe, if it is only necessary to bow low, and no medicine or support by ointment is worth it;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no other cure than work, and the vanity of the fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that one which is neither new nor old, hope for health by fire, as I have seen.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and keep the legs until they reach his buttocks, and bend his buttocks towards his belly
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then make an attempt to join the shoulder, or pull if there is pain, until you feel the bones line up or until he moves.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	if the patient feels pain at the root, then you must bite down on your thumb,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	He feels that it has been grasped; or whether it is uncovered or he feels between his shoulder blade and his hip, then his limb is broken and it is certain.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not slip away, it cannot be healed.</start_of_turn>
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We can easily mend all these things, but this is not the case;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that we give makes it, if it is grasped as we have said before concerning the size of the fistula; otherwise...</start_of_turn>
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And the remainder of the boil comes out through the fistula, as long as it comes from below the foundation; make this once or twice, until you know that these boils that are like a fishbone must be burned, which are similar to a quill.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Then the cure of soft pus comes out with the burnt hair, as long as the hair is still soft; then the cure of ointment is applied with oil and bandage.</start_of_turn>
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is well done, it is good. But if not, it will not be well;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if he tries to pass [the dislocated joint] between [other bones], and does not pierce through to the root which is or is like a foundation, and between the root and the attempt a thick covering of hair or flesh, and you see the fistula to that which adjoins the covering like a wound.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the head of the fistula comes loose before the attempt, and is held fast before the attempt, and the cautery is done afterwards, as long as it comes up to the head of the attempt;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the attempt will be delivered, and will be healed; then bind those hairs which appear like a feather of an owl, and there will remain nothing of them.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it does not please you, and if you are in doubt between the two things, if the fire cautery or the medicine is strong.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For indeed the fire cautery brings together three bones: namely, the scorching of these cartilaginous joints, the bursting of blood and the drying of moisture.</start_of_turn>
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of soft wounds covered with pus or broken bones, so that as long as these bones crack, the fire will burn them in the wound.</start_of_turn>
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the swelling with dry herbs, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes right up to the bone, and is pushed out by the flesh, if the bone or the foundation is loosened, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between the flesh there is bone, fat or cartilage, or if it is near piercing, if there is no other way out but to hope, by the administration of one of these three remedies:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you press it out until it is flat, or if you wish you can put in some attempts and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too far inward, for you must cover the dwelling that holds the foundation, and come out in the direction of the will of the lord.

puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then defend this wound which is in the wound, as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the lower part of the foundation: if it is a less severe matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	Then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the lower part of the foundation: if it is a less severe matter for the patient. And in no case are fistulas like this: and it is when you bite at the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs the skin under the foundation or extends outwards
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	...if it is a less severe matter for the patient. And in no case are fistulas like this: and it is when you bite at the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs the skin under the foundation or extends outwards if you take a perceived attempt at the root like this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	...and you must hold the attempt at the root all the way through the fistula until it is at the shoulder.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If the limb is bent at the root of the foundation, then grasp the thread of that which is broken, so that you swallow your thumb or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	Grasp the head of the thread and reunite the broken bones one with the other, and strain them against each other, and leave them in that position for a while or two.</start_of_turn>
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And do not restrain them at any time, until the thread has coped these bones that are between the two, and has become quiet.</start_of_turn
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.</start_of_turn>
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not break through, if you force it to break in every way you can, it will not be too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to force it with stitches if it is deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is sound.</start_of_turn>

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Emorrydes are in two ways: when they are deep-seated in the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are both small and large ones, and they cause pain and blood to seep outwards without any dressing.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more of them, and they push out the foundation and the head of the limb; but those which are pushed out have too much moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and are more feared of falling out, and often they are lost of life.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have it in the foundation, if you command the patient to sigh out to the chambers, while the foundations are still firm, and they open wide;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and you hold them with nails, or you hold them with your finger, then you must press them back into their roots.</start_of_turn>
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot be held by their moisture, if you take them with gauze, or cotton wool, or a piece of chammelon cloth.</start_of_turn
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out to your shoulders, then press them back in, and dust with warm powders that are in lieu of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or you shall cauterize if it is as it is said or in the treatise of cautery, and then treat with other remedies while he is well;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	Or if the foundation cannot be grasped, if you bite the patient with a biting and rough clamp to uncover that which is or is the foundation, if it can be grasped openly.</start_of_turn>
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	The patient cannot be held, and if the thread is fierce from the foundation, if it is the leg cure;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And that you take it at your finger or with tweezers, and hold it, and then treat as we have said, while he is well, and that he avoids the incision with iron.</start_of_turn>
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you consent that you bring the bandage in this manner: take one thread, pierce it with a needle, then pass the thread underneath and pierce the needle from the other side, and twist the two threads that are left on the needle.

des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in this chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.

et assemble les levres;	and assemble the limbs;

et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	And take an awl or more, according to the quantity of the wound's size.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then leave the head of the wound clean, that is to say without dirt, and insert an awl or there is a thick thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two holes of the leather with the two holes of the awl,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is soaked in the leather from within, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	And gather the hair of the armpit, the armpits together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain with a doubled thread around the needle of three parts.</start_of_turn>
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and gather the hair of the armpit, the armpits together;
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then leave one inch of space and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then the like of a needle did it just as the first time,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	then the like of a needle did it just as the first time,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the pain is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are blunt between soft and hard,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	For the subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and the too large if they do not enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be blunt.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not be forced too deeply into the flesh and leather
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	because they tear and open the wound before it has healed;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	Then cope the heads of the needles, so that they do not pierce the patient at night.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths over the heads of the needles to hold them in place,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	for this manner of stitching is more convenient in small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For there is often a thorn or something sharp.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second costure is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you join the ribs of the skin with the ribs of the flesh together with a thorn or there is a thick thread in the middle.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these bones all together.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you leave it in at the part where you began, in that way you will tear the guts.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place between the ribs the thickness of a nut of mace;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this rib will hold the flesh,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I shall sew up a wound like this one, which has been there a long time or is fresh.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	Who was the master of a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	who had a wound greater than the palm of his hand,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and had intestines well almost as wide as two palms,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I will restore the intestine when it has been gone for .xxiiij. hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will keep the wound closed until it has healed for 15 days, and I will care for it, and it will be healed.</start_of_turn>
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they thought that the patient would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	I did not treat him with any medicines, because I was in a place where there was no medicine available
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the way to proceed more above the wound is this: once the spur has begun, and the flow of honey-water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or thus I shall tell you three proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and pass it through from the underside up to this depth;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the knot on the right side, if you see the flesh slip or swell or if you have pulled the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And let the patient perceive from another part of the inside until it escapes;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And he will understand this order as well as a peelmaker does pelts.</start_of_turn>
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And let him leave once the scab from one side, and take it back from the other, until the bone is completely healed.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	As for the second method of curing, Galen does it quite well,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If it is thus as if no one has made it, who assemble the limbs naturally together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and join the one head of the limb to the other head in a natural way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or pin near the neighboring bone, and pierce only that one slightly,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	leave the other bones of the limb intact;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then draw the needle and make it pierce from the back part until it reaches the belly,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as indeed often do the bones of the face.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then draw through and pierce from the back part until it reaches the belly, alongside other bones of the face such as the cheekbones that are on either side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common method of treatment.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The witnesses are lying, and no one can prove it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must sew up the belly with three needles, or there is a thread in the flesh.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and the stitches that when the wound is turned out,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If it is more painful to suture than with other wounds on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judge of the wound is if it is such as the judge of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you stop the bleeding and the pain; then put on the healing powder and charcoal dust,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if it has moved from its place, do not put any weight on it until the wound has healed.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tighten the thread and keep the wound closed and still;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound like the others until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, put on something, until it begins to bleed profusely, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And the limb moves again the third time as much as it is sound.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you must not seek any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make common cause with the principal limb,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if you must moisten coarse linen with warm oil, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And put the thumbs inwards, and loosen the toes;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or decay in the belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the clusters of black wine swell up and the decay comes right up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and the teeth, and the large intestines, if they are fatter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestines which are called "the jejunum" cannot heal when they are swollen.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	This is due to the swelling of the veins, the brittleness of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	If the wound is stitched too tightly, if it is returned behind the intestine while still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is yellow or black, if you see that you should bind the black part, without delay, because bleeding does not cease from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For in this matter there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then consider that which is between the bone,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	put the joints hanging from the lower part of the wound until they are out of the way so as to align the extraction when the nails are withdrawn, and the wound is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la routure dou boueil	because of the wound's swelling.

Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closed, I doubted that the patient had not suffered badly in his belly.</start_of_turn

et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they say that whenever there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be ligated in a timely manner.
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take forceps and grasp the large intestines, then gather the layers of the wound together.</start_of_turn>

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If this happens in the intestine, and there is no other discomfort to the patient,

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Wounds that open or burst, when the covering is peeled off, if it is called universally 'fistula'.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and the same when it is cut and rent through
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to the truth when it is properly sutured and white, or there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is just as cut as the quill of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And never in a clear jump, or sometimes widely;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	And never in a clear leap, or sometimes widely;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I speak of it in the section of wounds, that every wound that is not sanitized and there is pus,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is only due to eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This is to know, by a slight prick of blood or flesh.
ou por sa malice;	or by its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hardness within, and on the bones, that does not allow new growth to take place.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much bowe;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	When the limb is put forward, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not very good in the treatment.</start_of_turn>
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is like a pestilence.</start_of_turn
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because in this part the digestion is late, and the health is late, and escapes by nature.</start_of_turn
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already mentioned these causes, signs, and treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you should know that I will tell you about the cure for fistula, which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Soaked as fistula has in all limb with pain;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the spleen, or the intestine, or the bladder, or to some of the bones,

et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not come out until I have said it, and you have promised to do the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you will see that it is right, if you take an attempt to drain or cauterize, if the fistula is complete;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is tortuous, if the edge of a subtle attempt to plug it,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if they burst through the hands and you cannot keep them closed even with stitches,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the bladder is burst through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture is very cold from one hole to another, and makes the body limp;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then when the wound is clean and the patient is awake, you must know if there are bones or nerves involved, and if it is suspected that they are pierced by an instrument.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press your hand, and the location of the pain.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for certain the location of the wound or the source of the pain, whether it is close to a joint, a nerve, an artery, or a vein,

si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	If you take example and aid in your work. There was once a youth of about thirty years of age who had pain in his leg due to something that was inside the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the matter came to the leg, and there was an abscess that did not appear for no apparent cause;

Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I made an attempt in one of these wounds, and then closed all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one wound had found the other throughout the whole limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I was forced to cut in one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And the wound was corrupted and smelled, and it went as far as the bone inwards;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	And I saw that which appeared to me from the bone corrupted, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for that which I had seen.</start_of_turn>
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound from medicines so strong by long tension, and I could not soothe.</start_of_turn
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the corruption continuing in the bone, the marrow, and then the bone itself, and I was compelled to solder the limb.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could do no more than I could bear until I saw a piece of the bone break through, and the marrow burst out whole
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicine; and he was healed and bound up soundly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and did not dare to do it again for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And because of fear of death that I avoid for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often blood is evacuated, but he remains whole,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and sometimes from the bone a hard scale is born, and is well disposed and causes no pain or hindrance in any way, neither to the upper part nor to the lower part.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any limb, if you know how to cure it in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Pren bien l’liéen, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take hold of the limb firmly, and strain at the head of the bone that opens, and command it not to extend upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another layer of linen cloth over the skin that is beside the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the limb, so that if you pull out the corrupted flesh from the socket,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And uncover the shoulder socket above the limb or you see hair, so that the hair does not stick to the socket.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put a sponge or a towel soaked in vinegar under the bone to cover the corrupted socket.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And cover so much hair as we can see and feel the corruption, and hair once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if he uncovers the whole joint; then put one thumbstone down,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	if he uncovers the whole joint; then put one thumbstone down,
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, bind the bone or what it contains on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, if there is no other angle except that of the cover;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if corruption is from the hand or from the wrist, if it is very painful,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but in any case you must inquire about the origin of that corruption, how it occurred to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and do everything in your power to prevent it from harming your vein or nerve;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and the rags that are cut and the threads that cover these bones are many, according to the size of the bone and the appearance of swelling.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their greatness and their slenderness, and their magnitude and their mineness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason it is prudent to appear at the sight of the work like an instrument of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and the tools that the work will show you, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you think the instrument is capable of it, according to what it is intended.
dou feu	If you think the instrument is capable of it, according to what it is intended for
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture, or by pressure, or by violence;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated the inflammation with medicine, it does no good,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	If it is necessary to support the limb up to the root or if the decay comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by that of death, or by malice, which is greater, the fault of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards comes the decay of the limb from limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And grasp with all your might; if you hurry too much,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if there is percussion from venomous creatures, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and others like them,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	then the corrosion is at the head of the bone, if you break it, and do not give it space to come until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	and if it comes up to the hand, if the break is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, if the bone catches in the flesh; and if it slips from the flesh, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And it is of no avail to use violent measures except for the amount of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do everything just as when the corrosion comes or the bone: if it comes to the first joint, if the bone follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes from the bone or the flesh, if the bone goes through the flesh;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it reaches the knee, if it touches the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the knee, if there is nothing else wrong but for the patient to be dead with it.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and if you bind or bandage the limb so that it cannot move freely,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	extend one hand over the other from below, and the other over the other from above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you shall separate the bone that is between the two joints with one span wide, as long as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you shall grasp or hold the bone, and put a bandage of lint on one side so that the bone does not touch the sound tissue.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and come to the patient another wound and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	and if blood comes when you work, if you cauterize the tissue sufficiently,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Or thou shalt put upon some restraining powders; then return to thy medicine until it be accompanied.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the limb firmly with a convenient bandage, and cure it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there was once a man here.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackening that seemed like fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And that corrosion first arises in its cavity of bone, as much as it consumes the whole bone.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	When the bone is seen to be corroded, if it is covered with copper and is sound;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corrosion returns or the hand comes again, it comes to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put upon it things that impede the corruption after the purging of the pus, and I cannot stop the corruption;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he swore that I should break his hand, and I would not dare to hope to recover the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And I doubted too that if I cut off his hand, he would not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he fainted, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and when he had covered his hand, and was cured.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have heard of no other treatment for fire burns except for this one, when it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	There comes no swelling in vain to the flesh, and it lingers as long as it makes great swelling of the limb.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and breaks through, and in the process breaks the limb, and keeps the bones bruised; like a vessel
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is under is also as subtle as a delicate veil of silk
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And do not touch me until the bone, until the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And are not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone embedded in the marrow, it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if you cover it will be like that of a drape;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have sworn that the skin will be corrupted, and the corruption is not in its depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick of hair, if the surgeon is skilled in blistering:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	regards if it is large, and if there is an unpleasant odor from it,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then the cluster of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Then take basil, oil, and mastic, equally, and mix them together in a vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And in loosening the skin, and straining the part;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine in place for an hour and a half, then take it out while stretching outwards.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this three times, until the skin is soft and flexible, and the bone is weak.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	never with water of tears.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	When this remedy is not present, and you take charcoal from the bottom of a vine, and drink cold water,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then loosen the bowels, and drink in a tumbler, until you feel that the pain has gone away;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear the pain, neither the Egyptian medicine of charcoal does it alleviate the pain,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	or if there is a little bit of bruised barley in a tumbler of water or honey;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	Or thou clistiriz with honey and wine mixed, that the honey have property to soften and cleanse.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the blood thin;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have sworn that the flesh is well softened,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clinking of that which is done makes the flesh burst out
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And it is that thou takest plaster of diaphinit, and makest it with rose oil and in wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or thou shalt anoint it with certain medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken their properties or treat them with unguents.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if it is slightly pierced through the skin is painful, and the ointment cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if an iron has pierced it, and puts in an attempt of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or when the basal bone is swollen, as it is elongated.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, if the nail and the socket leave too much swelling, the clot or the abscess can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening of the wound is below the navel, if the edge or more is lower than it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	for when the belly is pierced, if it does not leave behind a mark;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you do not cover your beard as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	it will appear in such a way that the hair curls downward to the lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the hair is parted, if you do not keep it covered,
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	you will see it all coming out again.
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If the limb appears suddenly: let the limb bend gently forward, and do not leave anything of the limb behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to bring relief to the chest.</start_of_turn>
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and cover the chest with one and a half cloths of linen.</start_of_turn
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then press as hard as you can toward the opening of the chest, which is more open than before,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	After that, the swelling is soft upon one side like another drape, according to the quantity of blood that has escaped.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it upon the wound to align the swelling, and do not remove the great swelling immediately, but leave it for a while;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is coming out from the wound, often stops by resting the swelling,

et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not.

si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	If the limb has shifted from another position, and is renewed.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it sustains a violent pain that does not subside after a while, its bones split and do not rejoin.

car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for there are people who are late in their enjoyment of food in their wounds, and some who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if it bows improperly and leaps from the joint after a moment, the nails of the joints do not bend but remain whole.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	If the nails of the bones do not break but remain whole, and if the joint has become loose and hangs limp, if there is an excess of moist and dry medicines in the body...

pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take oil of rose and rosemary in equal parts by weight;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then he must confirm and use it; and this very thing makes honey thicker and more viscous.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when oil is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh, aloes and incense, grind them, and sprinkle them over the honey when it is taken off the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then mix in one drape, and stretch it out, and never administer for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And the root of the celestial lily, which is also like flour sometimes and a hundredth part;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And in the use of simples or compounds: grind them up, make a powder of them, and mix with honey as I have said, and use it.</start_of_turn>
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this remedy.</start_of_turn
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then soak the body so that the corruption is softened, and make an impression in the bone, or has stiff limbs, or has swellings;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the surgeon of fistula treatment, as we said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the incision of the abscess.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is a swelling that arises from the socket of the arm, in the pouch of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or due to pain, or by chance it occurs in other ways;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	And when it is envious, and we take no care, if it comes to a boil, it bursts open like a wound.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	Then it breaks and flows out as much as it can, and by chance it breaks all;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to the bone, causing great pain; and the limb is pale and swollen
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If you must compel the shoulder to stay in place, remove all superfluous matter that is hindering its movement.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then burn the wound afterwards.</start_of_turn>
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help when the bone is intact, and the nail is sound.</start_of_turn
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the marrow and begins to swell, and the blood vessel bursts,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	If you think you can mend the dislocation with your right hand, do not put your left hand over the knot that the pain points to.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and hold the shoulder firmly and gently,
