puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bandage the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the decay is in the bone, if the socket is fractured, and the marrow is extruded, for as much as the corrupted bone is, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the bone fractured, if the socket is fractured as before mentioned,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the bone must be set so that it can heal;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is bruised and bloody, and there is great pain, it is necessary that you set it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then grasp the knot of the spleen acutely by cutting through below,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then grasp the knot of the spleen acutely by cutting through below,
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is anything that will soothe him.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be taken away.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Two thumbs are born in the hands of some men by chance, and are always fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is a part where there is bone, and never a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born in the root of the joint, or their birth is in some other place.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	he who is born at no time must not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of him who is fleshed is slight, in part like this:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the size of him is like the root of a large spindle.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grieved to cure: if you hold him under cover.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	When he is born or must later depart, if you must copy the round head first up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then copy the bone to a suitable length for this one, and then hold it until it is whole again.</start_of_turn>
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from birth, or from wound, or from burn, or from other things.</start_of_turn>
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you must copy that wound, if it must be repaired according to its natural form;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, that they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of soft sponge, as long as they are stuck together, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	It comes to nothing of its two palms with the palm of the hand, if it sticks together like that.</start_of_turn>
Des vils	Villages.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large vessels enclosed by fatty substances filled with melancholy humors, which arise in greater numbers with pain in the limbs.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often appear in those who walk and work and bear burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give her any purgatives, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of fire is as follows: with the copes and by driving out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And thus too, if you have closed the vein and applied pressure, draw out all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	If the limb is large, do this first: elevate the limb high up, until the blood vessels become taut without being ruptured,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip bone up to the lower part of the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then hold the vein for one, two, or three loops, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then believe and grasp firmly the black blood from your hand, from the thumb to the little finger, as many as there are without causing the patient any further suffering.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it, and command him to hold still, keeping the black bile enclosed;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and cause no harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The nourishment of this method is as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then he puts it out or washes it, and he raises the affected limb high up until it turns red, and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, if you burn the area with fire, and then hold the area over the vein for a long time at the shoulder or in the foot area at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then he covers the skin with ointment, and tightens the vein from below the thumb, until it turns white when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you will see it red and black, and when it enters or the skin seems like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then stretch the limb again, until it is freed from the skin, and then put a bandage on the wound,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then stretch the limb again, until it is freed from the skin, and then put a bandage on the wound; then pull the skin over the vein until it appears open,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then stretch the limb again, until it is freed from the skin, and then put a bandage on the wound; then pull the skin over the vein, if you have done so, and put a bandage on another one, if you have done so before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then stretch the limb again, until it is freed from the skin, and then put a bandage on the wound; then pull the skin over the vein, if you have done so, and put a bandage on another one, if you have done so before; then stretch the limb again, or several times if necessary, and then pull the skin taut,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then the trail and hold until the second degree; then remove the degree by degree, until it is all gone, then close.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not draw it out and lift it, if there is a splinter in all its fibers,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and draw it, and if there are nails there, break them to the root, and hold your hand from one side and the other, until they are gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and do not close it, for if you close it, if you cannot draw and lift it, and it comes to harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished treating it, if you draw out the limb from the wound covered with soft wool in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the limb is contracted and twisted and bound together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	So you must break it gently, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron from which the limb is bound is curved, and do not cut, that it does not touch the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:
De la voinne civile	It is of great concern, for if it were slight, it would burst the vein; but as we have said, let it be large. This is its form:
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there is no vegetation, and in the earth or where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it arises in other parts except the limb, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decay of the leather,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If he comes from the belly of the serpent inwards and outwards, grasp between leather and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if there is a sign of great swelling in this vein when it comes into the limb,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then its blood flow is choked, and the vein swells as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the limb is open, if you must you cover around a piece of lead from a third to a third of its length, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	et laisse le plonc pendant à la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en est point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nouvelle.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and leave the hair on the limb, and every time that it is pointed at the end of its growth, if the covering encloses the hair and the new growth, do not cover the root until it is completely grown out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns into the hair and causes swelling or pus, and sickness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because it must be treated thoroughly from root to tip, and nothing or foreign matter must remain.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de cinq palmes de longueur, ou de dix.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and never is this vein when it is treated with five palms of length, or ten.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if there is discharge from the matter within; and bring forth medicines that are healing and let them stay in place so that no inflammation results, and then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	and never is this vein stained with blood, even when it opens at the joint of bone or bone.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes out from a wound, and from that it leaps; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And it comes out from a wound, and from that it leaps; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	And it comes out from a wound, and from that it leaps; cure it therefore as we have said before
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And it comes out from a wound, and from that it leaps; cure it therefore as we have said before.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And he feels all around with his senses, from limb to limb, as long as he can see or he walks, and jumps with fear.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And he is tormented by the discharge of humors, like veins and serpents and worms and belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and he doubts of his malice, for when he goes through the body and reaches the head, and comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it sometimes returns, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and treating, if one cannot drive it out until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must hold the limb firmly above and below with a strong and firm grasp.</start_of_turn>
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	and if it is pierced by the nails of the bone, and you do not drive it out,

et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it makes is when it breaks the oil, as we have said.

De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from moisture.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "Vakirir," and is a pain that comes in the joints of the limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and because it moves from limb to limb; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and discovered her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And thus afterwards, the limb will rise up as quickly as a worm on the scapula.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, as quickly as if alive silver when it breaks from its root;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that limb and settles in the scapula,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and thus afterwards corrected throughout the body, until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back inside the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed to hear how it twisted back and forth within the limb, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I would rather maintain that pain in the limb is better than to move it to another place.</start_of_turn>
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not believe it, as I have seen it in women;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought that this was the reason why the woman had dry clothes and uncovered veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of that appeared that cold air was constricted;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear like this to me on account of those who are sick, who have dry clothes and uncovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	When you see the cure for this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the joint above and below has been strained, and then comes to rest upon such a constraint that the limb is constrained by force;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	force it to rest; then cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the antidote for these winds, as foul pills and serpin pills, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Des saiettes	From napkins.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The bandages are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they cause.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are various kinds of bandages, some having large points, others small, some with hooks, and some with sutures.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	some with angles, others with tongues, and some with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	or in the principle limb it pricks
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	If the brain, head, liver, spleen, pancreas, intestines, bladder, and similar members are affected.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes, then in no limb of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must know that you must take care of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward with many disorders.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, if the surgeon persists, and heals the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of a fracture when the arrow pierces the bone, and leaps the substance above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scraping, swelling, vomiting and bruising, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixture of senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes without a wound, or an ear; and often causes the speech and voice to be lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and sometimes a white moist wound resembling pus, and also like burnt charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If such a sign appears to you, if you persist in your treatment, draw out the arrow if it is not ensnared.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it tears or curves is that it is near the left breast, and feels just as if it were embedded in something hard, do not leave it empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow moves just like a pulse, and in black blood, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then there is doubt that the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the wound that never swells is only without streaks of blood spurting from the wound, and the swelling is inflamed, and the patient turns pale, and breathes high and stops eating.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks within the covering of the wound, if it is left in, it causes great swelling and pain and breathing; and the limb becomes rigid
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow breaks or is swallowed, by chance there is no digestion of the meat from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow breaks or is swallowed, and in the leap there is no passage of faeces from the intestine, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the stone of the bladder breaks and the urine spurts out and comes out with great force, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it be done and the cheek and the jaw and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the shoulder blade and the loin and the thigh and the foot and the limb mentioned above, is well disposed in many ways.</start_of_turn>
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the stone is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, for this reason that you do something else.</start_of_turn
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There is in the house one stone which is thrown or dripped at the root of the knee.</start_of_turn>
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and the traitor on the other side untied the fat of the ear, and it was cured without a scratch.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And the traitor brought out a pin that had fallen into the fat of the ear, from the earwax that had been loosened.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the pin was returned, and did not touch anything except for the tip towards the head,

Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from the side of the head, which was hanging down or in the belly, and thought it was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after three days, when it did not recover its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the bowstring, and the tendon, and the flesh, without any mishap.

Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And there went an arrow into the face of a prince of the king, who was sitting in the middle of the noise,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and his face was declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I flee called to the treatment after that it was closed for two days. If I find the wound very inflamed.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I would like to keep it all very quiet and do not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it caused him great pain in his ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was an arrow wound
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place upon the limb a plaster of adhesive digestive, so that it does not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I see the limb free from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the bandage again, and closed the wound, and comforted the patient for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow still inside his wound; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the corrosive medicine to the wound with my hands, as long as it is not overdone.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and keep the eye, and feel the head of the splinter that is coming out at the root;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I apply the medicine to the wound opening by that very medicine, until the splinter appears visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and left it well finished for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then stretch if the wound that I bound with nails, and hold it from one side and the other, and I cannot bear it any longer.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore I will stop tormenting and contriving in various ways, as long as I take it in hand. Indeed, if the nails are well made,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	In this way, when I have finished with this chapter, you will see how I will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it immediately, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or tell me about the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your remedy on what I do not understand, because the book does not teach me that;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you know the masters well enough concerning many great things, and concerning what is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Trueve neuf Chapitre, et neuf instrument, audescendment des choses étrangères qui surviennent dans cet ouvrage.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	Nine new chapters and nine new instruments; ascending from the strange things that happen in this work.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	... or by loosening from the limb or by some other means.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	... and that which is broken by moisture or which enters, is the marrow in the bones, and it breaks never again now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it as long as the hair is carried towards the root, and rejoice at its issue.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot be pulled out, if you leave it alone for a few days, and move it slightly each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will come out, and if it does not come out, if you pierce around with all sorts of instruments, as long as the wound is widened, and then pull out the nail.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the splinter is stuck in the bone of the shoulder blade, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And concerning any accidents that I have mentioned above: if you do not treat them immediately, but leave them as they are until they are even again after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the wound comes up to the bone, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	then it comes only to the bone, and does not reach the surface of the skin
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and leaves the patient with these days without any other accident, if it is able to be treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is firmly fixed and cannot be moved, if you administer tarterises round about, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the limb is bent back towards the body if it cannot be seen, if it has all its might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if the limb has no visible support;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you do not take hold of the wound, and by the depth of the wound,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	then take out the arrow if you must, and if there is an ear in the arrow, hold it so that it stays put.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone which is fixed with a thread is pulled out at the root that you must pull,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or crush the ear of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take care that you do not break the splinter, but rather grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not manage it once, if the limb remains entangled, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding contradicts your treatment, if you recall what we said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	take care of the incision of the nerve and of the vein, and put in place what you will use to grasp the splinter without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Or burn or cauterize, or with force or with ease; and set the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest help that there is, and if you do not know how, if you do not take heed of what he signs that he shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where one sees it or feels it immediately:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Thus do so long as the nails can take hold, and then take it out: if it is now necessary.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be displaced, if you leave it in place, and then resume the extraction until it comes out forcefully.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a splinter of bone left, if you see it, hold the limb firmly;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is a crack, and you see it, administer the limb immediately, if you administer it with a pointed instrument,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the point of the arrow enters the hole of the instrument; and then you must force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If the arrowhead gets caught in the hole of the instrument; and then you must force it out. If the arrow is deeply embedded, you must insert the instrument with the pointed end entering first, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	If the arrow is surrounded, if you must, remove all the surrounding tissue or the poison has spread, if that is what you suspect,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then cure the wound if it is necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if it is known that the splinter has penetrated the skin or the palm of the hand or the belly or the bladder or the ribcage, and it is close, cover over it immediately if possible.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	cover the wound and the nerve, then remove the splinter, and then close the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	leave it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the nails with which we treat the saiettes is similar to the beak of an owl, and thus is this form:</start_of_turn>
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, small, and medium, according to the amount of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the end of the shoulder is just like the quill of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to push out the splinter, if it is like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tweezers to push and to grasp if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common colour
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins of common colour
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	From veins of common colour
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	From veins of common colour
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And thus veins which are in the armpits of the eyes, which are called "aspire",
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the back of the ear.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two armpits which are under the arm.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the veins which are on the sides of the mouth, which are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And thus veins that are swollen to the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which we commonly see swollen are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is dark towards the left breast, and is called the great vein;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the brachial, which is composed of the cephalic and axillary veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it the vein of the head 'the vein of the heart'; and if it is burst or burst at the edge,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the vein of the head 'the vein of the belly'; and it is above the shoulder blade.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one from which one often sees, which bursts openly on the belly
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	and the saving one is the vein which is between the elbow and the wrist, and if it rains;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the limb or the palm of the hand are two veins: one if it is struck by the corbicula of the little finger of the left side costs,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And in the limb or the palm of the hand are two veins: one if it is struck by the corbicula of the little finger of the left side costs,
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are two veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to remove old blood clots, and to expel;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of the patient, as I have said, is that you must rejoice in the chief of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the skin or the veins are rough; then stretch the patient’s neck with a hook.</start_of_turn>
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the veins open behind the ears depend from the chief:</start_of_turn
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then do the nails of your thumbs and wherever you feel the pulse of your thumb, if it signifies an embolism.</start_of_turn>
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet, and hold the vein open with your thumb to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and hold the vein open with your thumb to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein, and grasp and loosen the skin and the vein well; it must be enough to pierce through, and make blood spurt out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then take the lancet, and hold the vein open with your thumb to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein, and grasp and loosen the skin and the vein well; it must be enough to pierce through, and make blood spurt out until you see it; then strain and tie it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And as for the incision and the cautery, or the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	the blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the blood of the brain is so.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient extends his neck, so that the two veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse throbbing in his thumb, and then he signs himself with the index finger.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then he holds the thumb over his vein in the upper part of his thumb, and he grasps the lancet from his thumb base,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and he holds the vein high up, and closes it, if like you have done with other veins, and do the evacuation of blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then the thread comes, and you leave it until it is whole; and we have already spoken of its handling and extraction, or its beginning in a book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood of the vein of the front is worth as much as the blood of the cephalic [vein] for old head diseases, and for migraine, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and if the patient twists his head too far, until the vein bursts
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called the "forceps," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold firm with your hand, or something else, and let blood flow out as much as you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient’s collar and bind the vein until it is firm and never open with a wide flame.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable for me to say that the flame should be too strong; and the same with the other side, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the veins that are in the armpits is of great help in these matters, and for the swelling, and for the pain, and for the stiffness, and for the fainting.</start_of_turn
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And if the patient strains his neck by twisting from side to side, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the same, and let the blood flow freely, a lot like a long flame, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make an incision of the blood, as much as you are able, and then ligate the vein, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not worth as much as water, and for sores, fevers, and illnesses of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If there is swelling and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and if the patient has a cold that causes them to cough, then strain their arm on their left hand.</start_of_turn>
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	take the long flame of the cautery and hold it between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open easily, and it will not open now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far in the wound, and draw out blood according to your need; then bind it for the night, for it is moist and restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the three fingers helps to loosen the spleen, to initiate the mixing of medicines, and to cure diseases, and to stop itching, and to corrode, and to cause herpes, and to reduce swellings.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the blood is that when the patient pulls out his head from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	Or let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient sit upon the seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then take the vein long and widely, and hold the blood vessel steady, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same in the other vein, and remove the ligature, and gently stretch the veins
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.</start_of_turn>
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms and shoulders helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and toothaches and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the limb, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the limb and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are known by this, that they are black, and because they have small black veins running through them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore one must seize them both, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if the larger one at the shoulder joint and all the blood vessels below and beside it are cut, for that is a dangerous method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the blood vessels below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and that is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and if the quality of the patient is such that the patient screams between his hands before the sun, and he stretches out the tongue, and looks towards each side of the cost, he will see a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then he must take hold of one and the other, and do not go too deep, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins often treated for inflammation are usually healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking with a blunt needle at every mark, or by cautery with a thin flame, as with trenchant cuts, and is called “anesil.”
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the size and thickness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the cautery is known to be mild, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And he must be skilled in opening the great veins filled with blood that appear full of blood and trouble.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier the small veins, or there is small yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments such as those of the throat, and the collar, and the foot, and the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The patient must remain calm and carefully watch the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he seizes the artery and blood spurts out, if it is necessary to hold it, as I have said before;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be overly cautious, but should seize it like an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	and if the vein does not open immediately, if you must, grasp another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or you wish no rain from him, or you keep hold of his vein in his arm: it opens immediately.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the fire cautery, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see that the blood vessel is burst, if you must at once pull the arm away, that you touch the flesh until you know the pulse.</start_of_turn>
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the limb, and then bind the arm, and hold the vein to the fire cautery.</start_of_turn
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	Beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the limb swollen, for it is the artery: stop immediately.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	When you see it swell up like the urine of a child, and it is pale and limp, know that it is not an artery: stop immediately.

se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	keep your arm still, and leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and if there is doubt or fear, do not move until it is safe.

And if it is not stained, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts open, for the head of the shoulder retracts; and close it off without delay.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a hold of the fist, and make a loop, and take hold of one of the halves and bind it well up to the other jaw;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it is not stained, that is good; but if not, if the doctor says so, as we have said, powders that stain blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the staining is not much in greater quantity in various situations because of the small quantity of the wound, and the position of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood in the vein helps to stop the bleeding from the head and the chest.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basal and cephalic veins, as we have said before;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	it is useful for the safety of the nerve that is below, and if it is not too deeply pierced, and if it touches the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	it swells and it suffers either wounds or by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The nerve is often opened multiple times; if it does not open in some homes due to its subtlety, you must know that you must cut away the surrounding tissue with an anesthetic instrument; and take care of the nerve at your leisure.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is of long duration.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it pulls blood away from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is better to cauterize with the olive flame or the mirtin flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerves nor arteries.

et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, if the limb swells up in some place, it is not necessary to do it on the first attempt, but grieve nothing.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must only be drawn for the purpose of maintaining health.</start_of_turn
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the blood be drawn from one of the two veins which are either the cephalic, the facial, or the basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and must wait a while before administering the antidote, and must feed and drink during this time, until the sign of swelling disappears;

Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood that is administered for diseases has no definite measure, but whenever need be urgent or necessary, at all hours and in every tension.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not permitted to treat the sick for more than 123 days, nor women who are pregnant for more than four months until the seventh month

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	and whenever anyone shall see a physician, in whatever manner, if it is commanded that he defend the intestines from a mild fistula,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a mouthful of phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw intestines over the superfluous parts that are nourished by the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither does it suffice that the limb is too swollen with flesh, that it is raw, so that it is forced, or hydrops, etc.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if there is a wound from the spleen, or vomiting, and swelling of the belly, and frequent vomiting of blood and other discharges, and this either by the violence of the weapon or poison;

et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then he massages the limb with his hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them there.</start_of_turn>

que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not bleed.</start_of_turn>

Leave then out of all that we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but make it [the wound] i.e. emplastre dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it to darken as long as it is red; and if you see it large, leave it to dry until it is subtle; and if it is too thick, let it cool down.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for the plain and robust person, who has the need to extract blood, to make the wound larger and the flame greater.

et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of bleeding is useful for the evacuation of blood and the relief of pain, and is more useful than if the bleeding were prolonged rather than intense.</start_of_turn>

Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood of the right elbow vein is worth more than all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method:

Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If you must do it a second time, do not do it immediately, because the limb is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and make the other side equal in size.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The thigh bone is at the ankle of the buttock, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that flows abundantly.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And its quality of blood is such that if the patient is between or bathed in it, it will strain under the ankle for three fingers when twisted.</start_of_turn
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it will not open; and if it does open, do so in all the ways you can, and by cutting through.</start_of_turn
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to leave the hair as it is, for the root is soft and easily slips back into place by the hands of a layman.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	If you do not hold it firmly, if any drop of blood should appear or if there is pain, and if you withdraw your hand a little, and take care of the wound;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make as much pressure with blood as you see, and then release the pressure, and put on a bandage and bind it; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuum therapy.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selon ces manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sang, ou sans ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Ventouses are made of horns, or hair, or wool; and ventilation is done in these ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.</start_of_turn>
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation which is done by cutting and drawing blood is done in twelve ways.</start_of_turn>
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	or it is at full heat, or it is at a moderate heat.</start_of_turn
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And thus with others on both sides of the neck; and the suction cup is applied to the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup is applied to the space between the jawbones; and the suction cup on the ears.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the suction cups embrace both arms; and the suction cups of both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cups of both ankles; and the suctioning does not affect any blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore let no man fear me, even as when we draw blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And therefore let no man fear me, even as when we draw blood from a vein. And I command that it be administered without fear, neither with great heat nor cold, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the limbs are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it be necessary to vomit, or for custom, if the administrator giveth some at the beginning of the month or at the end, and if he giveth too much at once, or too little, or if he giveth it too soon or too late, or if he giveth it too violently or too softly, or if he giveth it too hot or too cold;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	he should not make me shiver or fear, and should not make any movement of the mouth.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if such things happen to cause swelling and redness on the face, head, and neck, and the eyes are dull;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and things like that which cause a discharge of blood in the mouth, have driven out the tongue, and clot blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such things which cause pain, and see blood and sweat and moisture and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when moisture has come to the middle of the month, we command the patient to keep the wound covered for two hours more.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the physician helps for the grief of the head … that comes from the eyes, and it cannot be done until after the evacuation of all the hair.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this vomiting is in lieu of the blood of the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it cannot be done except in those who are pale of complexion in use, or who have a headache, for this causes them great discomfort;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it cannot be done except in those who are using it who have a cold fever or a cold disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who remains silent in such a state, if he becomes oblivious, it is necessary to place the ventouse somewhat lower down due to the doubt of obliviousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction cup at the collar is in place of the blood and fat of the chief and the marrow, and for this reason it is worth expanding downwards.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and at the fracture of the channel of the windpipe, and in all, and in swelling;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and one must push it back, for if it stays too firmly, it causes obtuseness or bloating of the belly or the side.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds blow cold from the coast, and causes chills of the head, and pain in the root of the teeth, and swelling, and constriction.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	This is in lieu of the blood of the basilisk; and it is commanded that the patient place his hand on the artery, that it does not obstruct the vein, and that there be no oozing of blood.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds blow cold from the coast, and causes chills of the head, and pain in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in lieu of the ailments of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds blow cold from the coast, and causes chills of the head, and pain that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the spleen are as valuable as two veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to feel too much pain, for the blood vessels are sensitive and know how to bleed
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the flank is as much as blood vessels under the foundation, and there are diseases of these, and it is advisable that the swelling be large and coarse, that it has mixed well; and by chance, if it were slight, if it should break, it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The hair of the legs becomes loose and wide open, because it attracts blood from all over the body, and causes an ancient pain of rains, and of marshes, and of the bladder, and makes swell the flowers; and is in lieu of two sophies and two calves, and all of them cause the body to swell afterwards for a long time, and bring about vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is that you apply it immediately when it is empty, and do so steadily, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing so until you see the blood flowing freely and swelling; then withdraw, and reapply the suction cup, and take care of the position of the body, for there are some who have too much hair, and pores that bleed: if you cut once only, you will cause great wounds and deep veins; and do so cautiously.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, if you must cut twice: the first time to remove the large blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If he does not moan excessively, if you may wound him for the third time; when our wounds trail blood so profusely, so profusely that our hands are stained a third time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	When our wounds trail blood so profusely, if we do it again; and if he does not moan excessively, if we wound him once more, and if he does not moan, if he feels it, it is finished when his wound is perceived to be cured.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is suitable for one who has thick skin and tough hair, and who has boils full of pus, that you order the loosening of the wounds with oily cataplasm that is dissolving and soothing
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if this is the case, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If it is in yeast, oil of cresson, or linseed, or chamomile, or something similar.

Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or of elderberry, and of thyme, and of similar things.

et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and does not feel well from the bath before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and does not sleep well after the ventosation.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and must be warned when he must vent and when he is vented.
