si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if you can give him cold things, such as grapes, radishes and lettuce at ease, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and give him medical wine, and broth of barley, and moist meats.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	and if he has a cold complexion, give him honey syrup, and fragrant wine medium, which is between elderberry and raspberry, and eat sparingly, and eat medical things and small oils and herbs.</start_of_turn>
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And when the wind blows, if it must more drink than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and you must give to some people no food at all, neither meat nor drink, before or after [the wind blows], in order to comfort the principal parts.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be discreet about it, but do not let anyone know who is to have nothing to eat or drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The winds that are put to the wound are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and under the belly and the groin and the armpits and the heel, for these members do not suffer from wound above these.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And do not force it, but only to draw blood from limb to limb.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	or if we put on the limbs when they do not wish to bleed; to overcome the viscosity that is in the limb, as when we put on compresses on the belly and the buttocks to make the limb limp;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves pain, when there is inflammation or a wound, for by its attractive virtue it attracts the inflammation or removes the wound from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so it is done when it is put on the liver and the mouse when there is retained moisture.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these compresses are administered empty with vinegar only; and never with fire, and never filled with hot water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	If there is swelling in diseases, and in such a manner that we must fill the compress with hot water alone, or with water or where there are herbs that adhere to this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the compress administered with fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two broad edges and half a palm in height, and has or costs a little hole in the middle, as if to push out a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be known, if the patient blows upon it beforehand, so that it does not bleed the patient when putting it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And hold in the middle a stick of wood or iron, to put a bandage firmly in place,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be great and small according to the ailment and the hardness of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the swellings of the limbs are different from those of the body, and the lean from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one put this sponge on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take hold of the skin or cloth, and put it under the edge of the sponge which is under the suction cup.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	if the skin tears at the bottom of the suction cup, it will burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and you must either be above or below the opening we have mentioned, if when you look you see vapor coming from it, remove the sponge.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take hold of the limb just as before, and repeat it often if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	And in the case where it is administered for the ailment of pleurisy, at all intensity, there is no bulge or perforation, and it is only administered when it is plain water, and is put upon the limb just as little;
et c’est li forme:	This is the end of the text.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without doubt, they are only administered in limbs or where one cannot put venoms because of their small size, such as books and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And on the limbs stripped of hair, whether by desire or by force, and other similar things.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the patient is such that when you touch them without feeling that the hairs are soft and smooth, if you pluck them out,
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	you must pluck them out, and put them in hot water that is lukewarm, until they are limp and soft, and have no pain in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then either bathe them in a vein and with a suction cup, and then scrub the limb until it is red, and put on the dressings;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are even and smooth, and if it is bone or we can put on a suction cup, put it on, for this is worth doing afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, if you lift the limb slightly, then sharply and with force, it will heal well, and then expel it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is left too late after the pus has dried, moisten it with a cold cloth of linen, and put on, until the wound is healed;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiplied, put on ground vitriol or alum, and similar things, until it is healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or thou takest out half of the hairs from the skin, and leavest them as long as they burn on the skin, if thou stayest now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Or thou takest out half of the hairs from the skin, and leavest them as long as they burn on the skin, if thou stayest now;
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the hairs do not come out easily, if rub the skin with fresh blood, or thou shalt insert a needle as far as it goes,
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, if they burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	When you see that they groan, if powder is sprinkled on a wound of aloes and gum, or charcoal, if they will groan from now on. Saith thus, dear friend, that this chapter contains things that neither ancient books nor learned letters have ever mentioned;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, it is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I know of nothing else, except by the science of ancient books, or because I have studied it so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the custom of my life
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described it in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book that it contains words and chapters which put understanding into the science, and teaches the truth, so that those who are proved in this science learn and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs to anyone, if you command the patient to hasten to the doctor on one side and on the other, if nothing else hinders him, even if he is weak of limb or young or old,
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if his tension is not very strong, or too cold; and eat only cold broth, that is to say cold juices, broth of herbs and broth of barley, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fat, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins with blood, until you have certainty of complete healing, without swelling or expansion of the limb.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, if you command that the patient be nourished with meats that cause great swelling, or if he has viscosity, as with millet dough in water, and wheat germ, and testicles, and spleen, and pancreas, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at this part of nourishment, the muscles relax and become more brittle.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken from marrow and decrepit do not mend well by themselves, according to their nature because of the drying out of the limbs, just as if they were of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no remedy, remain on the broken bone, that is to say, strong tension that has occurred and joined the limb together, until it is as strong as before; and do not let go of it at any point, for because of this we recommend nourishing with coarse foods, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the marrow, and others by cutting, as with the size of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the armpit there is its engine, and its proper instrument in the restoration, as it is remembered to come to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known by the breaking of the bone by that which its flesh is twisted, and opens well by force, and by the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no dislocation, and no great pain, the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no breaking;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but he can well have dislocation, or fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move your hand, but put on medicines that will come afterwards, and then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	If the joints crack that are in the armpit, and the two parts of the joint are equal, you must now put them in their place equally, even as if pus had come out;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if pus comes out, if you leave no wound, as long as the abscess is calmed down.</start_of_turn>
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it firmly, if it comes to that.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they extend to the palm of the hand or the wrist, or to the thumb if it is a small limb, or to the forearm or to the elbow; or two strings or a string and the thumb.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are loosened, if you leave them in their place, you must keep that in mind to prevent causing further damage or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join together well the broken fragments of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the dressing is good and is not too tight, do not press as they do who make come by their work to cause swelling and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at rest, if the patient is quiet and does not move, does not watch or sleep, does not twist or bend, in any way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take great care that the limb is so secure that it does not cause him any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, it is necessary to place it in such a way that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight so that no twisting occurs when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limbs are various in small and large size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and the like: if you cover them with a cloth of linen moleskin and soft,
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as bones and thighs: if you cover them with a wide and hard cloth, for the large cloths embrace the whole great limb and constrain it everywhere equally, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then you must tightly bind the limb, i.e. twice or thrice according to the size of the limb, and restrain your hand an inch above the break and loosen the break slightly, so that the break is released an inch from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb a little, so that you take a great part of the pain, then take hold of another limb, and tightly bind over the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then raise to the lower part of the fracture, and hold moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said at the beginning of this chapter.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the lying bands of linen or cloths, so that they are all even, and then bind everything up above. i.e. bandage, and then put your stakes well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, if put above soothing things to the abscess, which will harden the swelling, and leave it there for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your stakes, and let them be half as wide as a broad needle resting soundly, or of staff from which we make nails, or of barley straw, and let them be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the one who sets the fracture places a support under the break which is greater and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be of equal length as it is necessary for the limb in its entirety or in its girth.</start_of_turn>
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is strained upon the supports just as you did at the first hour, and then bind under a thread immediately, as it was at the first hour on the break.</start_of_turn>
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of flax.</start_of_turn
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I would wish to do some works of fools who bind their knots with linen thread, this is a great error, for the knot will not be even if it is too tight, and it will hold only if there is space between the knots less than two thumbs.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is numbed by the bites of the nails after stripping in the groin, if you put sponges of lint or coarse cloth on them, they will not bleed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bone fractured, and the bone is broken, I shall speak of the cure afterwards.</start_of_turn
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And those threads which he cannot bear to withdraw from these stars shall break all the bones of the first hour.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is great, he cannot bear to put these stars in it except after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound that comes out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and when the limb is great, he cannot bear to put these stars in it except after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound that comes out; and thus the ancient methods of packing restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that is held as by the walls of a mill, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and put this confection, neither too coarse nor too fine, and use it, for this is the common method of packing that restores the fracture in various positions, even among women and small children, for there is neither too much pressure nor too little.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of packing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and flaxseed and linseed and saffron and arabic gum and mugwort, in the amount of ten; myrrh and aloes, in the amount of five; chamomile, in the amount of seven and eight. Mix them together and grind them into a powder; mix this with abundant eggs. If the patient’s complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other means of displacement that is worth torsion: take mugwort and viscum, each ten; myrrh and aloes, each seven and eight; acaice five; Armenian bile ten, and grind well, and confit with water or a great deal of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other means of displacement that is worth torsion: take mugwort and viscum, each ten; myrrh and aloes, each seven and eight; acaice five; Armenian bile ten, and grind well, and confit with water or a great deal of egg, and administer. Other means of displacement with joints and bones loosened from their place, and relieves the pain that comes from it, and breaks down the swelling: take new lint, and moisten with oil and boil, and put on the wound. These plasters do not restore quickly, but they are good for soothing post-burn pain, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of displacement that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pell leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of treatment for the restoration of a broken bone and to mitigate the remaining swelling. Take root of mallow, chamomile, violets flowers, barley flour, and one part of chaff; grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with moist vinegar or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of treatment more forceful than the first, when the abscess hardens comes to the restoration of the limb. Take root of mallow and flaxseed, barley, melilot, and thistle, and violets and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for certain things that make wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two, not too soft or too hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have us put something dry and warm upon the broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and other such things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions or fennel seeds, and beeswax, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone of his limb is not displaced; if not, loosen by hand every day.</start_of_turn>
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain comes to the limb, or there is swelling, sense of rest or inflammation, if you hurry, loosen it and remove the obstacle now; take a light dressing, a sponge of salt in moisture, plunge into water, and raise up the limb until the swelling ceases and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry lint, soak in water or rose oil, and bind up with a bandage, until you are certain the bleeding has stopped.</start_of_turn>
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And rest the inflamed limb, and relieve the pain, then reset the bandage, and a little more of pressure, and do not strain it too much; and be discreet until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that at the incision point there are swelling, redness, pain, and swelling, then you must immediately stop and bind it firmly, as you did at the beginning.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not improve in the limb what we have said, if it does not loosen after two or three days, or five or seven; do not leave it for twenty days, as we have observed, until the swelling has subsided, and approach the position of the limb above.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore hold it more tightly than before, and swell the meat, as I have said before; and if you see the limb dry out more than usual, do not fear that its marrow will dry up;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Rose loud now, and thus with warm water, every time you loosen it, and this is whether from the first joint to the last, and kill a little of the tension;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Rose loud now, and thus with warm water, every time you loosen it, and this is whether from the first joint to the last, and kill a little of the tension; for in this work thus does the limb naturally rise up: that is bad, and if there is any doubt or fear, I see no other remedy but to leave it alone and treat it directly.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various forms of breakage</start_of_turn
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many fractures are of various types, and the causes are numerous.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are fractures caused by spear-thrust, and the collarbone fractured throughout the bone up to the sypha, which is the marrow cavity of the bone, as in the case of splinters or fractures; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «splinter fracture».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or if the spear pierces the bone in a reverse direction, this is called a «complete fracture»; and the wound of these fractures can be large or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	and if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the joint, or any other similar thing.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a fracture that approaches the joint that is below the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and whether the wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	If there is a wound that lies close to the bone as tightly as a nail, and the fracture is slight, it is called a 'capillary' fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is made by a pierce, or by a shard, or by anything similar, and if it causes the bone to split into two, as when coals are placed on a cauldron, if the marrow is between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This usually happens with bones that are soft and damp, like the bones of children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And in all these ways, small pieces break away from them if like stars; and I will speak of it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these ways of fracture from the separation above them, from tension, and from the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary mark is known by this, that when one has discovered the bone, and has rubbed fat on it, if the fracture is black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no other mishap, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, feverishness, and other similar things, if these do not heal, doubtlessly there is a serious underlying condition.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you see no imminent danger and hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you arrive in this state first, and it is in the armpit, then you must immediately remove the bone in front of the wrist toward the thumb
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you delay in removing the bone in front of the elbow toward the thumb, the tissue surrounding the bone will become corrupted, and there will be the accident that we have mentioned

Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief. Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through it, even though you administer nails with washers, do not pierce too deeply beyond the test of the bone; and must have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if the nails come out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have washers for all tests; and this is the form of the two manners of washers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put one washer on the bone, and turn your two thumbs until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the washer back in another place a little after, and do everything around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more skillfully than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have moved the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have if you have nails, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone, and treated, if it is possible, reset the socket which is dislocated from the bone to all other instruments which resemble an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tense and subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If it remains detached from small bones, no nails, if the bone is slightly damaged, then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the liquid is very strong, and that is its word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by displacement of the muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and hold the pointed end of this incisor lens, for this is its shape:

s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, if the bone breaks easily, because one must break the bone quite steadily, and with some sense.

And if the bone breaks without piercing the skin, cut the bone as little as possible from above; there are small pieces. If you can, return the toughness and remove the scales of the whetstone that you must have in various quantities, to bring about in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.

En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle fractures, it is convenient to bring about the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>

puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drapeil doubled in half or in quarters, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first drapeil; and do it more gently than you would, that you do not damage the scab, then administer another layer of lint, and do not strain it more than is necessary to hold the wound only.</start_of_turn>

et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus. de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no break of the skin, the fracture is often incomplete, not completely broken through, except for the fragments within, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the lower part, to bite down with the index finger of the opposite hand in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take hold of the index finger of the right hand, and grasp the fracture lightly, and move it apart with the other hand by force, and hold it equal
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., it is necessary to administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes swelling, or if a tooth is strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken mandible cerote on and put on a pair of double drapes; and put on a large bandage well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and bind it on the tooth as you wish, and command the patient to rest, and eat lean meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the limb is deformed, if the bone is fractured at the third part, and then reset it in its place; put on a plaster cast with fine powder of beeswax with plenty of egg yolks or flour of alum, after you have broken the cerote; and put on a clean bandage, and if the plaster casts have dried, and the limb does not move, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it is healed in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if there is swelling in the apostemes, if we have already said many times.

Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if the edge has burned according to your necessity.

And when you have boned all these pieces, and there is no more movement, if the wound is wide, put on some covering over the wound, in order to prevent infection, as long as it is necessary.
de la forcele	because of its force.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forced fracture occurs often before, behind the shoulder, and if it is broken and loosened in two pieces, there are fragments, and it is the lightest to restore; or if there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the fracture is with a wound, if you have two assistants, let one hold the limb that feels the forced fracture; and the other extend the head towards the part; then put the fracture back in place, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of wax, or linen, and be large as you need; and extend and hold the forced fracture, and strain the ball at your hand, so that you can put the fracture back in place as it should be.

If you do not manage to support the head of the humerus in its proper position, because it comes out of place, you must know that the patient lies supine on his back, and put the arm under the armpit, namely the middle armpit, and keep the minister there until the head of the humerus is raised up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find fragments, if you must, make an incision there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot reunite by any means, if the head has become fractured at one of the incisors that you have made; but that you put under the armpit the instrument which is called the forcele, to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and appears like a scoop, and is not very deep, and be as wide as it seems necessary, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the rule for the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit. Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensible to wounds and to the tailor, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of the yolk of an egg, and put on stockings loosely on, and put a splinter of lead under the skin if you must.</start_of_turn>
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great bandage of a palm of a broad width, and put two layers of cloth over the wound, and hold it in place; then take a needle of moderate size, two fingers wide and long, and encircle that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains pendant.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Then put the needle on the bulge, and twist the bandage over the shoulder, and drain the fluid from the sore, and drain the fluid from the painful side; and hold the shoulder firmly, and when you see that the ligature holds the bulge steadily, and you see clearly that the needle does not move from the fractured bone, if you reward every jerk, and when you see that they are slack, if you restrain them.

de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and keep it still until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to anyone.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and keep it still until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to anyone.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it is on top, and the bone, do as we have said in the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess above.
de la brisure dou pis	If a piece of bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it is on top, and the bone, do as we have said in the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess above.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The limb is never broken in the middle, but this often happens; but it often breaks from violence. And when it is broken in two, if it declines to the side, and causes the patient great pain, and swelling, and vomiting, and by chance evacuates blood, and opens the wound in the broken bone, and one feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and slightly force them equal in every way that you can, until the limb is as it should be; then put on dressings and stamp with the thumb a little salt or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind tightly to the bone, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round behind, and strain gently, and reward chest every hour the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you see that it will not hold, because of corrosion or purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, do not delay, but loosen and remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the way of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and slightly force them equal in every way that you can, until the limb is as it should be; then put on dressings and stamp with the thumb a little salt or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind tightly to the bone, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round behind, and strain gently, and reward chest every hour the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you see that it will not hold, because of corrosion or purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, do not delay, but loosen and remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the way of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fractures of the ribs only come from great blows to the back and the head, and they do not swell except for these things which are slippery; and one can well know at the inquiry how they are.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier. And if the fracture of the ribs is downward, if the patient feels great pain, and swelling, as with pleuracy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and there is swelling, and vomiting, and great loss of blood, which is a serious matter, and the former has put on great pain.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it is necessary to administer nourishing foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to break the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for those who are unconscious or dying.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there is life in them, let them be conscious.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one should put on stockings over the limb, because of swelling; for this is similar to reason; however, there is doubt that the stocking will hold back the excess fluid from the limb due to weakness.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, and put on tents between the ribs to make the girth even, then either cure the pleurisis, meat and medicine.</start_of_turn
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points the rib, and there is doubt to the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in dressings, namely instruments to hold the face; then it must be cut through the bone, and treated gently, and then the two layers of the wound must be sutured, if it is large, and it must be cured with sponges, until it is healed. And if pus comes from the wound, if you put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the wound; and treat while the bone is being held in place, and if necessary above the rib, until it is healed.

Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a fracture of the rib bone, and often it rains; and also at the shoulder blade.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this occurs to no avail, and you know not whether he will be saved or not, if you take heed if you see his hands limp and fleeing and dead, and that they cannot move or extend, and if you prick them with a needle, if he does not feel. Such is death in many positions, and if you move him and he feels well when you strain and point, such is the joint of the bone saved, and the patient cured, if we put the cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when such things come to pass at the spine, and you know not whether he will be saved or not, if you take heed if his limbs are softened and his accidents are those which are in his hands, and upon his back there is sudden wind and vomiting with aversion; and when he has been cured upon his belly, there is sudden vomiting with aversion. And when he has been cured upon his back and he sees the vomit, if he cannot bear it. Such is death: if he faints in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these things do not occur, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the remedy is that if there is a wound at the base of the hair, put upon the spine oil of rose or oil of nutmeg of an egg, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comfortable and drying plasters, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone is dislocated, if you can cover over the limb; and unite the two ends of the wound, if it is large, with a bandage, then cure with oil that binds hair, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "fracture of the jaw", if it is on your left hand, and put it equal to the right hand at your waist, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you must; then strain, and if there are broken bones, if you leave it like that, and unite the bones, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	and the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if there is no sign of improvement despite prolonged treatment, and if it is rejected by the flesh, it brings pain to the patient, swelling, and causes the fractured part to bulge out.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the fracture is high up, when you extend your hand over the fracture as long as you are over the break; and you mark what is fractured and how it is positioned; and if the fracture is only at the hip, if you make it even, as long as it is in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is low down, or if it slopes outwards, make the patient lie on his belly, until the fracture is restored.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you put on the shoulder, then put on a staff of wood or bone, and hold the arm steady, so that it does not move; and keep the limb still, as long as the limb is even.
