Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If after the joint is reset, it still feels painful, and moves, bathe and gently massage it, pressing until the pain subsides; or put a poultice of mutton fat on the joint, and leave it in place for a day and a night, then extract the poultice, and reinsert the limb.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If it sweats, gently dry the joint, then put the poultice back in, and then enter or bathe; and do this several times until it is healed; if you notice that it returns to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than any other joint in the body. It is necessary to restore it to its place immediately, even if it is loosened, and even if there is swelling or a wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And its restoration is that you place the affected limb on a table, and extend the limb, and look that it is even, so that it places its palm on the surface of the joint, and hold it until it returns to its place
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, it is necessary to watch if it is well placed; then put the patient’s hand back on the table at extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, make the patient place the back of their hand on the table and their eyes their hand on that part of the joint. If it returns, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the relaxed muscles after the incisions is too great, loosen the stitches and let them recover in their natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot bear it, and you do not wish to put it back in place after a few days, the limb will remain dislocated.</start_of_turn
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and do not cause him any pain except that which the hands themselves suffer; and do not attempt to move or extract anything: because if the nerves are severed or the arteries are cut, nothing else is worth doing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you put on the plaster we mentioned before, then strain and leave it for three days, then take it off and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well, and if there is no pain, if the joint is swollen with warm moisture, then massage it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	until the dislocation of the shoulder of the arm is healed.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the fingers of the hand detached at the wrist, never at the back of the palm or the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	When it is thus, then take hold, and hold the dislocation steady until it returns to its place; then support the head of the bone that is joined, and guide it toward the part where it is connected.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	When it has been thus, then hold it for a while, and then set it straight; and do not bind it, as we have said, but support the limb so that it does not move, and do this often until it is firm again.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same in the case that the dislocation has been dislocated at the root of the limb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same in every case of dislocation
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient is in danger.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the sign is that the evacuation of the urine flows in the opposite direction, it cannot be held, and many times is softened no limb, or the knees or the arms or the legs.</start_of_turn
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the scapula is moved to the third part; which is called "gilbosite."
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The wound is cured when the cause of the swelling has disappeared from infancy: if no cure or healing can be found.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from blows or impacts or similar things, say the old methods of treatment with great words, or there is no great benefit to it;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes before, there is no remedy or healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And thus also when it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except for that which comes from behind, as I have said.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And thus also when it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except for that which comes from behind, as I have said. And let the patient keep his face even in one eye, and hold the eyelids apart, so that they do not close.</start_of_turn>
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then take hold of the thumb at the base of the wrist and the other hand has a piece, and bind a thread loosely around the patient’s waist, and another around the hips, and another around the thighs, and another around the calves;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two assistants know the threads, one at the head and the other at the foot, among the thumbs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well closed, as we have said, and look that he puts his palms on the spine, so that it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a thumb and two fingers long, and press the area below the abscess, and let the patient lie on his side, and hold the head of the thumb below the abscess, then place the middle of the thumb on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and put his palms on the other head of the thumb, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not work, do it with the nail that pierces the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And take two thumbs at the head of the patient’s arm of great length, and over the two thumbs, have between each thumb a sow and an ounce, a long space;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And in each basin there is one hole, or the nut is loose, and the basin is firmly fixed in the earth, so that it does not move; and between each two basins there are one hole. There are in each two basins one nut returning, so that the string returns, and there are in each two returns two small nuts of the length of a thumb, to return the nut.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then the thread which is between the whorls at the nut towards the head, and the other thread towards the pieces at the other nut, and between each two basins the master turns his nut to the whole thread, and the master puts the spindle even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put upon plaster desiccant with abundance of egg yolks, and then press, and then support with a tablet of two thumbs of length, which prevents the swelling of the swelling and the soft part of the vertebra, and then bind with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient’s natural nourishment, until it is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if nothing comes to pass at the end of the illness, if it is recommended to administer soothing and relaxing medicines, with the proviso that we have said before; and in no case shall one administer a piece of lead.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And never let the appearance of a swelling on the back of the neck be mistaken for a dislocation; for it is the bone that has burst, from which we must not presume anything: for by chance there comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder never come loose except for simple dislocations, never if there are other joints; and the joint of the hip is damaged in three parts: front and back, and front and back; and the more front it is damaged, the more it is damaged in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And he knows of his dislocation when, if one joins the painful limb with the limb above, if it is longer and opens more the pain of the patient than before, and he cannot double his knee over the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And thus is the cause of the loosening of the limb from its socket, for in this case the head of the shoulder comes loose from its place.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.</start_of_turn
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this is that if the limb is well placed as it should be, although one may see him make a movement of his knee without pain; if this is seen, one must prevent it, and withdraw the urine, and swell the area, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And the sign of that one who has behind him, if he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and his limb is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and he has pain from the hip down to the toes
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three methods of dislocation, if you are hasty and turn the joint, and stretch outwards and downwards, and move forward and backward; by chance it will return, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, if you must know, summon a strong minister, and keep the limb firm at both ends, or at least as much as is possible, until it is bound over the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another minister grasps his hand under part of the manner that he holds his hands down by his buttocks, then he ties it with a strip of cloth over the hip; and another holds the head of the limb steady.</start_of_turn>
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains so.</start_of_turn>
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three out of four cases; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, if you must make a cure for its semblance. Then let it hang from the top of a staff, or on the ground with the two arms stretched out; then command the minister to grasp the head of the shoulder, and let another minister hold the patient, who graspes the shoulder, for the joint is now returned smoothly.</start_of_turn>

And rest for two or three days, then loosen, and put in the support above; and if you see that they are even, if you strain as before, and leave it. de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation from the shoulder joint.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is emptied in two ways: that is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards; and do not empty it forward.

de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the shoulder bone.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The bone is never whole, and never fully dislocated, but is always somewhat bent and fractured.

puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the eyes evenly on the dislocation at its joints, and another assistant grasps the limb firmly at the elbow, and the dislocation will return immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it has settled at a point, if you put on a pad and compress above, and strain the limb, and bind the bone to the limb, and keep the nerves above the ankle behind, so that it does not become too tight.</start_of_turn
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for one or two days, and if the strain has subsided; then loosen the binding at a third or a fourth, and tell the patient to walk for three days.</start_of_turn
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	If he approaches that limit, it is not my certainty that he will not suffer further damage.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he persists in this state, if you must restrain him, as we have said elsewhere, until he is well again.</start_of_turn>
des dois	until he is well again.</start_of_turn>
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if you can manage them well, it is a light matter.</start_of_turn
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not in any knot of the shoulder or the arm, then you must make the patient sit upright on a chair or a table, and place your hand on what is open of these joints, then push your hand forward until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When it is even and there is nothing open, if you put the root of the arm on a chair at the height of the armpits, then push forward, and hold for two days, then release; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Together with wounds and dislocations.</start_of_turn>
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you do not show humility in the treatment, and if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and timely, do not be proud;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use calming things at first, bandage the wound, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you now restore the limb to its place, even if the swelling remains;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is at rest, if necessary, administer calming things around the wound, and cure the wound, if possible, with dried herbs.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	If there is a fracture with dislocation of the bone ends, and if the bones are broken, do what has been said in simple ailments.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	Beware of entering a state of fear, as I have said, for this will bring you harm according to your Creator, and for the saving of your soul and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Explain the physical symptoms.
